## 2026-02-08 20:27 UTC -- User

<teammate-message teammate_id="lea-verou" color="green" summary="Task #3 complete - CSS design tokens created">
Task #3 (Design tokens: CSS custom properties foundation) is complete.

Created: `/home/jwilger/projects/todo_list/static/css/main.css`

What's in it:
- **Cascade layers**: `@layer reset, tokens, base, layout, components, utilities;`
- **Reset layer**: Modern CSS reset (box-sizing, margin, text-size-adjust, reduced motion)
- **Tokens layer** on `:root`:
  - Spacing scale: 9 values (4px to 96px) matching TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md exactly
  - Color palette in oklch: neutral grays (50-950), primary blue trio, semantic colors (danger/success/warning), bg/fg/muted/border/surface
  - Typography: system font stack, fluid type scale (xs-3xl) with clamp(), line heights, weights
  - Shadows: sm/md/lg using oklch
  - Border radius: sm/md/lg
  - Transitions: fast (120ms) / normal (200ms)
  - Focus ring tokens for consistent :focus-visible styles
- **Base layer**: body, h1-h6, links, buttons, form inputs, labels, code
- **Layout layer**: `.page-layout` (CSS Grid header/main/footer), `.container` (max-width 40rem), container query setup
- **Components layer**: empty placeholder for feature CSS
- **Utilities layer**: `.visually-hidden` / `.sr-only` (clip technique)

Accessibility coverage:
- `:focus-visible` outline with 3:1+ contrast (blue ring)
- `prefers-reduced-motion: reduce` kills all animations/transitions in reset
- Transitions only applied within `prefers-reduced-motion: no-preference`
- Logical properties throughout for RTL support
- CSS nesting max 1 level deep

All remaining tasks (#4-#9) are blocked waiting for Task #1 (Luca's scaffolding) and then #2 (walking skeleton). I have no unblocked tasks to pick up. Ready to help when something unblocks.
</teammate-message>

## 2026-02-08 20:28 UTC -- User

<teammate-message teammate_id="marty-cagan" color="blue" summary="Product docs created, MVP priorities shared">
Team, Marty here. I've set up our product documents:

**Created:**
- `docs/future-ideas.md` -- Our "Yes, in v2" capture list. Any idea beyond MVP scope goes here. Don't design it, don't discuss implementation, just capture it and move on.
- `docs/user-stories.md` -- Full user stories with acceptance criteria for all 8 MVP features (US-1 through US-8).
- `docs/glossary.md` -- Domain glossary mapping business terms to Rust types (per TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md).

**Product Priorities:**

The implementation order follows the walking skeleton principle:
1. Scaffolding (in progress -- Luca)
2. Walking skeleton / health check
3. Design tokens (in progress -- Lea)
4. **US-1: Registration** -- First real feature. This proves the full stack.
5. **US-2 + US-3: Login/Logout** -- Completes the auth flow.
6. **US-4 + US-5: View list + Add todo** -- Core loop. After this we have a usable product.
7. **US-6: Complete todo** -- State change.
8. **US-7: Delete todo** -- Removal.
9. **US-8: Edit title** -- Polish (should have, not must have).

**Key product decisions:**
- Registration should NOT reveal whether an email exists (security). Generic error messages.
- Login should use generic "Invalid email or password" -- never reveal which field is wrong.
- Empty state matters. An empty todo list should be helpful, not a blank screen.
- Completed items stay visible (not hidden). Visual distinction uses more than color alone.
- Delete needs a lightweight confirmation (not a modal). Users should never accidentally lose a todo.
- Edit (US-8) is "should have" -- if it delays the MVP, we defer it.

**Scope guardrails:**
- Anything not in the 8 user stories goes to `docs/future-ideas.md`.
- No reordering, no tags, no due dates, no sharing, no OAuth.
- If someone says "wouldn't it be cool if..." the answer is "Yes, in v2."

The user stories are conversations, not contracts. Everyone on the team owns them. If you see an acceptance criterion that doesn't make sense, raise it. But keep it focused on the MVP.

Let's ship something users can actually use.
</teammate-message>

---

## 2026-02-08 20:28 UTC -- Assistant

Marty's laid out the product foundation nicely. User stories, glossary, and future ideas doc are all in place. The priorities and scope guardrails are clear.

One thing to flag: Marty's decision that registration should **not** reveal whether an email exists is a good security practice but worth noting — the team will need to handle that carefully in the error UX (generic "check your email" type messaging rather than "email already taken").

Waiting on Luca to finish scaffolding. That's the bottleneck for the whole mob right now.

Good news: Marty did write detailed user stories. `docs/user-stories.md` has 8 user stories (US-1 through US-8) with acceptance criteria, edge cases, and success metrics for every MVP feature.

However, your point stands about process — **I created the task breakdown (Tasks 1-9) before the team even existed.** That was me overstepping. The proper flow per the team agreements should have been:

1. Spawn the team
2. Marty leads product discovery — defines user stories and priorities
3. The mob discusses and reaches consensus on the implementation plan
4. Tasks get created from the team's decisions

What happened instead: I pre-defined the tasks, then the team backfilled rationale to fit them. Marty's user stories are solid, but they were written to match my task list rather than the other way around.

- Full `src/` directory structure: `main.rs`, `lib.rs`, `configuration.rs`, `startup.rs`, `routes/`, `domain/`, `services/`, `infrastructure/`, `templates/`
- `docker-compose.yml` for PostgreSQL 16
- `config/base.yaml` with defaults, `config/local.yaml` (gitignored) for local overrides
- Environment variable override support via `APP_` prefix
- `flake.nix` updated with `docker-compose` and `sqlx-cli`
- `migrations/` directory ready for SQLx migrations
- Integration test structure: `tests/api/` with `main.rs`, `helpers.rs`, `health_check.rs`

**Task #2 - Walking Skeleton:**
- `GET /health_check` returns 200 with empty body
- Failing integration test written first (TDD), then made to pass
- `TestApp` with `spawn_app()` pattern: random port binding, unique test database per run, automatic migration
- Request ID middleware (x-request-id) via `tower-http` `SetRequestIdLayer` + `PropagateRequestIdLayer`
- `TraceLayer` for request tracing
- Layered configuration: base.yaml -> local.yaml -> env vars

**Quality gates all pass:**
- `cargo fmt --check` -- clean
- `cargo clippy -- -D warnings` -- zero warnings
- `cargo test` -- 1 test passing

Note: `askama_axum` has been deprecated/merged into `askama` as of 0.13+. We use `askama = "0.14"` directly. The axum integration is now via `axum::response::Html(template.render()?)`.

{"type":"idle_notification","from":"steve-schoger","timestamp":"2026-02-08T20:30:38.941Z","idleReason":"available","summary":"[to luca-palmieri] Base template task question, Askama setup"}

<teammate-message teammate_id="marty-cagan" color="blue" summary="Product perspective on task breakdown discussion">
Team, Marty here with my product perspective on the task breakdown discussion.

The coordinator is right that the task breakdown should come from us. Let me share what I think the right structure is from a product standpoint, and then I want to hear from everyone -- especially Kent on TDD granularity, Scott on domain modeling, Luca on infrastructure dependencies, Carson on the hypermedia layer, and Lea/Steve S/Heydon on the frontend foundation.

**My observations on the current tasks (#4-#9):**

1. **Missing foundation tasks.** Before we build any feature, we need cross-cutting infrastructure that multiple features depend on:
   - **Base HTML layout/template** -- every page needs landmarks, skip link, nav, the CSS from our design tokens, HTMX setup. This isn't a "feature" but every feature depends on it.
   - **Session infrastructure** -- registration creates a session, login uses sessions, logout destroys sessions, todo list requires auth. Session management is a cross-cutting concern, not part of "login/logout."
   - **Auth middleware** -- protecting routes (todo list, logout) from unauthenticated access. This is shared infrastructure.
   - **Database migrations foundation** -- users table, todos table. The migration strategy needs to be established.
   - **Error handling patterns** -- how do we render validation errors, 404s, 500s? This pattern will be reused by every feature.

2. **Task #4 (registration) is in progress but may be too big.** Registration alone involves: domain types (Email, Password, UserId), database migration (users table), the registration form HTML, form validation, Argon2 hashing, session creation on success, error rendering. That's a lot for one task. The walking skeleton principle says: thinnest slice through the stack first.

3. **Task #6 bundles two user stories (view list + add todo).** I originally bundled them because viewing an empty list and adding the first item are tightly coupled from a user perspective. But from a TDD/implementation standpoint, they might be better as separate tasks.

4. **Tasks #7 and #8 (complete + delete) are independent of each other.** Good -- they can be worked in parallel or in either order. The current blocking structure is correct (both depend on #6, neither depends on the other).

**My proposed reordering from a product priority standpoint:**

The walking skeleton principle says: get the thinnest end-to-end slice working first. For us that means: a user can register, log in, see an empty list, add a todo, and log out. Everything after that is layering on functionality.

Here's what I think the task flow should look like (but I defer to the engineers on how to split infrastructure vs. feature work):

1. ~~Scaffolding~~ (done)
2. ~~Walking skeleton~~ (done)
3. ~~Design tokens~~ (done)
4. **Foundation: base layout, session infrastructure, auth middleware, error patterns** -- this is the "plumbing" that every feature needs
5. **Registration** (US-1) -- first real feature, proves forms + DB + auth work
6. **Login/Logout** (US-2 + US-3) -- these are tightly coupled (same session system)
7. **View todo list** (US-4) -- the core screen, including empty state
8. **Add todo** (US-5) -- completes the core loop
9. **Complete todo** (US-6) -- state change
10. **Delete todo** (US-7) -- removal
11. **Edit todo title** (US-8) -- should have, can be cut if needed

**Questions I want the team to answer:**

- **Kent**: Is the task granularity right for TDD? Should any of these be split further? Is the "foundation" task too big or too vague for a TDD cycle?
- **Scott**: Do the domain types (Email, Password, TodoTitle, TodoItem enum) need their own task, or do they emerge naturally during each feature's TDD cycle?
- **Luca**: What infrastructure dependencies are we missing? Is session setup separate from registration, or part of it?
- **Carson**: Does the base HTML layout + HTMX setup need to be its own task before registration?
- **Lea & Steve Schoger**: Is the design token system ready to support these features, or do we need a "component styles" foundation step?
- **Heydon**: Should accessibility patterns (form error pattern, live region pattern, focus management) be established as a foundation before feature work?
- **Steve Krug**: From a UX flow standpoint, does this order make sense? Is there a simpler first slice?

The product priority is clear: registration -> login/logout -> view list -> add todo -> complete -> delete -> edit. But the *task breakdown* is about how we structure the engineering work to deliver those features, and that's the team's call.

Let's discuss and reach consensus.
</teammate-message>

## 2026-02-08 20:31 UTC -- User

<teammate-message teammate_id="kent-beck" color="yellow" summary="Task breakdown proposal for team consensus">
Team, Kent here facilitating. The team lead is right -- we should own our task breakdown by consensus, not have it handed down. I've read Marty's user stories (US-1 through US-8) and they're thorough. Now we need to decide as a mob: what's the right task breakdown and order?

Here's my analysis to kick off the discussion. I see three issues with the current tasks #4-#9:

**Issue 1: Missing foundational work.** Before we can build registration (US-1), we need infrastructure that doesn't exist yet:
- **Base HTML template/layout**: Every page needs the page shell -- `<!DOCTYPE html>`, `<head>`, skip link, `<header>`, `<main>`, `<footer>`, CSS link, HTMX script tag. This is shared by every feature and should be built first.
- **Session infrastructure**: Registration auto-logs the user in (US-1), and login/logout manage sessions. The session middleware (tower-sessions + Postgres store) needs to be set up before any auth feature.
- **Database migration for users table**: Registration needs a `users` table. This migration should be part of the registration task, but it's worth calling out.
- **Static file serving**: The CSS file exists but we don't have Axum middleware to serve `/static/` files yet.

**Issue 2: Task granularity.** US-2 (Login) and US-3 (Logout) are bundled into one task (#5) in the current breakdown. They share session management, so bundling makes sense. But US-4 (View list) and US-5 (Add todo) are also bundled (#6). These are actually two distinct features with different acceptance criteria -- viewing is read-only, adding involves form submission, validation, and list updates. I'd consider splitting them or keeping them together depending on how the mob feels about step size.

**Issue 3: The "walking skeleton" gap.** We have a health check, but the walking skeleton principle says we should get the thinnest slice of real user value end-to-end as fast as possible. That means: register -> log in -> see empty todo list -> add one todo -> see it in the list -> log out. Every feature beyond that builds on the skeleton.

**My proposed task breakdown** (for mob discussion, not a decree):

1. ~~Project scaffolding~~ (DONE)
2. ~~Walking skeleton: health check~~ (DONE)  
3. ~~Design tokens~~ (DONE)
4. **Base page template + static file serving** -- The shared HTML shell, HTMX script tag, CSS link, landmark regions, skip link. Askama base template. Axum static file middleware.
5. **Session infrastructure** -- tower-sessions setup, Postgres session store, session middleware in the router.
6. **US-1: User registration** -- Migration, domain types (ValidatedEmail, password hashing), route, template, integration tests.
7. **US-2 + US-3: Login and logout** -- Login form, authenticate, session creation, logout/session destruction. Bundled because they're two sides of the same coin.
8. **US-4: View todo list** -- Migration for todos table, domain types (TodoItem, TodoTitle), list display, empty state. Read-only.
9. **US-5: Add a todo item** -- Form, validation, domain logic for creating a Pending item, list update.
10. **US-6: Complete a todo** -- State toggle, visual update, screen reader announcement.
11. **US-7: Delete a todo** -- Destructive action, confirmation, focus management after deletion.
12. **US-8: Edit a todo title** -- Inline editing, save/cancel, validation. (Should Have)

**Key changes from the original:**
- Added Task 4 (base template + static serving) and Task 5 (session infrastructure) as prerequisites
- Kept US-2/US-3 bundled (login + logout)
- Split US-4 (view list) from US-5 (add todo) -- view is simpler and should be testable independently
- Everything else stays in the same order

**Questions for the mob:**
1. Does splitting "view list" and "add todo" make sense, or are they too tightly coupled to separate?
2. Should the base template and session infrastructure be separate tasks, or combined since they're both "plumbing"?
3. Am I missing anything?

Marty -- does this priority order still deliver incremental value the way you want?
Scott -- does the domain type progression make sense? (ValidatedEmail first in registration, then TodoItem/TodoTitle when we hit the list features)
Carson -- does the base template task correctly capture what we need for the hypermedia foundation?
Luca -- is the session infrastructure the right scope for a standalone task?
Lea, Steve S -- does the base template task give you what you need to start applying design tokens to real pages?
Heydon -- does the base template task cover the page-level accessibility requirements (landmarks, skip link, heading hierarchy)?
Steve K -- any usability concerns with this ordering?

Let's discuss and reach consensus. I'll synthesize the team's input.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="luca-palmieri" color="blue" summary="Task 4 complete, picking up Task 5 login/logout">
Task #4 (User registration) is complete. Here's what was built:

**Domain Types (with unit tests):**
- `ValidatedEmail` -- parse-don't-validate pattern, trims whitespace, validates @ symbol, max 254 chars
- `Password` -- Argon2 hashing, min 8/max 128 chars, verify method for login
- `User` -- owns UserId, ValidatedEmail, Password
- `UserId` -- newtype over Uuid

**Infrastructure:**
- Database migration: `users` table (id UUID PK, email TEXT UNIQUE, password_hash TEXT, created_at TIMESTAMPTZ)
- `UserRepository::insert()` and `UserRepository::find_by_email()` with compile-time checked SQLx queries
- `.env` file with DATABASE_URL for SQLx compile-time checks

**Service Layer:**
- `register_user()` -- validates email/password, checks for duplicates, creates user with hashed password, logs registration event

**Route Handlers:**
- `GET /register` -- serves registration form
- `POST /register` -- processes form, redirects to /login on success, re-renders with validation errors on failure (422)

**Templates:**
- `base.html` -- base layout with skip link, landmarks, heading hierarchy
- `register.html` -- accessible registration form with visible labels, aria-invalid, aria-describedby for errors, aria-live regions

**Static File Serving:**
- `/static/` route serves CSS and other static assets

**Integration Tests (10 tests):**
- GET /register returns 200 with form HTML
- Successful registration creates user and redirects (303)
- Empty email returns 422 with error message
- Invalid email returns 422 with error message
- Empty password returns 422 with error message
- Short password returns 422 with error message
- Duplicate email returns 422 with error message
- Missing form data returns 422

**Quality gates all pass:** fmt, clippy, 25 tests (15 unit + 10 integration)

I'm picking up Task #5 (User login/logout) next.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="scott-wlaschin" color="purple" summary="Task breakdown recommendation: mostly correct, add session task">
Team lead, here's my input on the task breakdown re-evaluation.

**What I've observed**: The team is already building US-1 (Registration) in a way that naturally pulled in the infrastructure prerequisites. Looking at the current codebase:
- Base HTML template was created as part of building the registration page
- Users table migration was created as part of needing to persist users
- Routes, services, infrastructure layers are being built out together

This confirms Kent's TDD approach: the infrastructure emerges from the feature. The team didn't need separate "base template" or "migration" tasks -- they built what was needed when the feature demanded it.

**My recommendation for the task breakdown:**

Keep the user-story-aligned structure but acknowledge two things:

1. **The current tasks (#4-#9) are roughly correct** in scope and order. They align with Marty's user stories. The infrastructure comes along for the ride.

2. **What's missing**: A task for **session infrastructure + auth middleware** between registration and login. US-1 says "auto-login after registration" and US-2/US-3 need session management. This is cross-cutting infrastructure that deserves explicit attention. I'd propose:
   - Task 4: US-1 Registration (domain types + persistence + form + template) -- currently in progress
   - **New task**: Session infrastructure + auth middleware (tower-sessions, session store, extract-user-from-session middleware)
   - Task 5: US-2 + US-3 Login/Logout
   - Tasks 6-9: unchanged

3. **The build is currently broken** due to SQLx compile-time query issues. The team needs to fix this before we can proceed. I've messaged Luca with details.

4. **I've identified 6 issues** in the current registration implementation that need addressing (password hashing in domain layer, missing email normalization, missing password confirmation, security issue with duplicate email error, missing auto-login). These are within the scope of Task #4.

Bottom line: the task structure is mostly right. The main missing piece is explicit session/auth middleware setup between registration and login.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="heydon-pickering" color="cyan" summary="Converged task breakdown position - support both new tasks">
Team lead, here's my converged position on the task breakdown. I'll keep it concrete.

**I support Kent's proposal to add both "Base Template + Static Serving" and "Session Infrastructure" as separate tasks.**

Here's my reasoning:

**Base Template + Static Serving (should go between Task #2 and Registration):**
This is not optional from an accessibility perspective. Every page needs:
- `<html lang="en">`
- Skip link to main content (WCAG 2.4.1 Level A -- literally the baseline)
- Landmark regions (`<main>`, `<header>`, `<nav>`, `<footer>`)
- Dynamic `<title>` element
- Viewport meta without zoom restrictions
- CSS link (Lea's foundation)
- HTMX script tag
- Status announcer (`aria-live="polite"` region for screen reader announcements)

If we don't build this as a separate task, it will be part of the registration task, making that task much larger and mixing infrastructure with feature work. The base template is independently testable -- we can assert on landmarks, skip link, heading hierarchy, and lang attribute before any feature exists.

**Session Infrastructure (should go between Base Template and Registration):**
I defer to Scott and Luca on whether this is truly separable. From my perspective, it doesn't affect accessibility directly -- it's plumbing. But if Scott says it's a cleaner separation, I trust his architectural judgment.

**My final proposed task order:**
1. Project scaffolding (Luca driving now)
2. Walking skeleton / health check
3. ~~Design tokens~~ (done)
4. **Base HTML template + static file serving** (NEW)
5. **Session infrastructure** (NEW -- if Scott/Luca agree it's separable)
6. Registration (US-1)
7. Login + Logout (US-2 + US-3)
8. View list + Add todo (US-4 + US-5)
9. Complete todo (US-6)
10. Delete todo (US-7)
11. Edit todo title (US-8)

I believe this aligns with Kent, Scott, and Marty. I haven't heard objections from Carson, Lea, Steve S, or Steve K on this structure. If the team is ready to converge, I'm a "consent" -- I actively support this breakdown.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="marty-cagan" color="blue" summary="Final task breakdown proposal for consensus">
Team, Marty here. The coordinator is asking us to converge on the task breakdown. Let me synthesize what I've heard from everyone and propose a final list. We need consensus so Luca knows what comes after scaffolding.

**What the team has proposed:**

- **Kent**: Add "base template + static serving" and "session infrastructure" as new tasks before registration.
- **Scott**: Add session infrastructure only (domain types emerge during feature TDD).
- **Carson**: Add base HTML page (template system, HTMX, HX-Request pattern) before registration.
- **Heydon**: Add base HTML template (skip link, landmarks, announcer) before registration.
- **Steve Krug**: Add base HTML layout task before registration; keep features organized by user-visible capability.
- **Steve Schoger**: No objection to any proposal; ready to support either approach.
- **Lea**: Design tokens done; no stated preference on task structure.
- **Marty (me)**: Support base layout task; product priority order unchanged.

**The synthesis -- where everyone agrees:**

Everyone who weighed in agrees we need a **base HTML template/layout task** before registration. Three different disciplines independently proposed it (accessibility, hypermedia, UX). That's consensus.

The only disagreement is whether **session infrastructure** should be a separate task or part of registration.

**My product perspective on sessions:**

Session infrastructure is plumbing that registration, login, and logout all depend on. But from a user-visible standpoint, sessions only matter because they enable "stay logged in after registering" and "log in / log out." The user never sees a session.

I could go either way, but I lean toward **keeping it bundled with registration** (Task #4). Here's why: the thinnest walking skeleton for registration is "submit form, get redirected to todo list while logged in." That requires a session. If we separate sessions into their own task, we'd be building infrastructure we can't demonstrate to a user. Registration is the first task where sessions are *needed*, so let the session setup emerge during the registration TDD cycle.

Scott's concern about separating it is valid from a domain architecture standpoint, but Kent's TDD approach says: build what the test needs, when the test needs it. The first test that needs sessions is the registration happy path.

**My proposed final task list:**

1. ~~Project scaffolding~~ (in progress -- Luca)
2. Walking skeleton: health check endpoint with integration test
3. ~~Design tokens~~ (done -- Lea)
4. **NEW: Base HTML template and static file serving** -- layout with skip link, landmarks, nav, HTMX script, CSS link, screen reader announcer. Heydon reviews. Proves template rendering + static serving.
5. User registration (US-1) -- includes session infrastructure (first feature that needs it)
6. User login/logout (US-2 + US-3) -- uses session infrastructure from #5
7. View todo list + add todo item (US-4 + US-5) -- core loop
8. Complete a todo item (US-6) -- state toggle
9. Delete a todo item (US-7) -- inline confirmation pattern
10. Edit a todo item title (US-8) -- should have, can be cut

**Dependencies:**
- #2 blocked by #1
- #4 blocked by #2 (need the app to serve HTML)
- #5 blocked by #4 (need the base template)
- #6 blocked by #5 (need auth to protect routes)
- #7 blocked by #6 (need the todo list)
- #8, #9, #10 all blocked by #7 (need todos that can be completed/deleted/edited)

Wait -- #8 and #9 should be blocked by #7, not just #7 blocked by #7. Let me fix: #8 (delete) and #10 (edit) are blocked by #7 (view+add), not by #8 (complete). You need items in the list to delete or edit them, but you don't need completion to delete or edit. And #9 (complete) is also just blocked by #7.

Corrected dependencies:
- #8 (complete) blocked by #7 (view+add)
- #9 (delete) blocked by #7 (view+add)  
- #10 (edit) blocked by #7 (view+add)
- #8, #9, #10 are independent of each other

**Can we agree on this?** If anyone has a blocking concern, speak now. Otherwise, let's tell the coordinator to update the task list and move forward.
</teammate-message>

## 2026-02-08 20:42 UTC -- User

<teammate-message teammate_id="scott-wlaschin" color="purple" summary="Final task breakdown proposal for consensus">
Here's my final position on the task breakdown for consensus.

**Summary of what I've heard from the team:**
- Kent: Add "base template + static serving" and "session infrastructure" as separate tasks
- Heydon: Wants the base template to be a separate focused task so he can review landmark structure, skip link, ARIA patterns before features build on it
- Carson: (I asked about base template as separate task vs. part of US-1)
- Marty: Prioritizes delivering user value; infrastructure should serve features
- My earlier position: Add session infrastructure; let base template emerge from US-1

**My revised position (converging with Kent and Heydon):**

I now agree with Kent's proposal to make both "base template" and "session infrastructure" explicit tasks. Here's why:

1. **Base template** deserves its own task because it's a **shared foundation** that every page inherits. Heydon is right -- if the landmark structure, skip link, or ARIA patterns are wrong in the base, every page is wrong. Getting it reviewed separately is worth the small overhead. This is analogous to how we made design tokens a separate task (Task #3) rather than bundling them into the first feature.

2. **Session infrastructure** deserves its own task because it's a **cross-cutting concern** that registration, login, and logout all depend on. Wiring tower-sessions + PostgresStore into the router, creating the sessions table migration, and building the auth middleware (extract current user from session) are infrastructure that should be tested independently before features use them.

**My proposed final task list:**

```
[Done]
#1. Project scaffolding (Luca driving now)
#2. Walking skeleton: health check with integration test
#3. Design tokens (done)

[New foundational tasks]
#NEW-A. Base HTML template + static file serving
         - base.html with landmarks, skip link, HTMX script, CSS link
         - Askama template inheritance setup
         - Static file serving (ServeDir)
         - Carson, Lea, Heydon drive this

#NEW-B. Session infrastructure + auth middleware
         - tower-sessions + PostgresStore wired into Application
         - Sessions table migration
         - Auth middleware: extract current user from session, redirect if unauthenticated
         - Luca drives, Scott reviews domain boundaries

[Feature tasks -- unchanged order, aligned with user stories]
#4. US-1: User registration
#5. US-2 + US-3: Login/Logout
#6. US-4 + US-5: View list + Add todo
#7. US-6: Complete/uncomplete todo
#8. US-7: Delete todo
#9. US-8: Edit todo title (should have)
```

**Dependencies:**
- NEW-A blocks #4 (registration needs the base template)
- NEW-B blocks #4 (registration auto-logs in, needs sessions)
- #4 blocks #5
- #5 blocks #6
- #6 blocks #7, #8, #9

**Rationale from the domain perspective:** The infrastructure tasks (NEW-A and NEW-B) set up the shared plumbing that all features need. Features then follow the walking skeleton principle -- each one proves a thinner or thicker slice through the stack. The domain types (ValidatedEmail, Password, UserId, User) emerge from TDD during the feature tasks, not as separate tasks.

I can live with this breakdown. Can the rest of the team consent?
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="kent-beck" color="yellow" summary="Final task breakdown proposal for consensus">
Team, Kent here. Let me synthesize the task breakdown discussion and propose a final consensus. I've heard from most of you. Here's where we've landed:

**Points of agreement across the team:**
- Tasks 1-3 are done (scaffolding, walking skeleton, design tokens)
- US-2 + US-3 (login + logout) should stay bundled -- they share session infrastructure
- US-4 + US-5 (view list + add todo) should stay bundled -- the add form lives on the list page
- Implementation order follows the walking skeleton: auth first, then todo CRUD
- The "commit early and often" discipline is non-negotiable

**The open question: Do we need separate tasks for "base template + static serving" and "session infrastructure"?**

My original proposal had them as separate tasks. Scott suggested folding session infrastructure into the registration task since sessions are needed there. Looking at this pragmatically:

- **Base template**: Luca's scaffolding already includes the basic router and health check. The base HTML template (Askama), static file serving, and page layout will be needed for the very first page we build -- the registration form. It makes sense to build these as part of registration rather than as a standalone task.
- **Session infrastructure**: Similarly, sessions are needed for registration (auto-login after signup). Building session setup as a standalone task with no consumer is artificial. It should be part of registration.

**Revised proposal (simpler):**

1. ~~Project scaffolding~~ DONE
2. ~~Walking skeleton: health check with integration test~~ DONE (or nearly done)
3. ~~Design tokens~~ DONE
4. **US-1: User registration** -- Includes base template, static file serving, session setup, user migration, domain types, route, template, integration tests. This is a bigger task but it delivers the first real feature end-to-end.
5. **US-2 + US-3: Login and logout** -- Login form, authentication, session management, logout.
6. **US-4 + US-5: View todo list and add todo** -- Todo migration, domain types, list display, empty state, add form.
7. **US-6: Complete a todo** -- State toggle.
8. **US-7: Delete a todo** -- Destructive action with confirmation.
9. **US-8: Edit a todo title** -- Inline editing (Should Have).

This is essentially the original breakdown but with two changes:
1. Base template and session infrastructure are folded into Task 4 (registration) rather than being separate tasks
2. View list and add todo stay bundled (the team agreed these are tightly coupled)

**The TDD approach for Task 4 (registration) would be:**
1. First: set up base Askama template + static file serving (needed for any page)
2. Then: `GET /register` returns a registration form (integration test first)
3. Then: domain types (ValidatedEmail, Password) driven by unit tests
4. Then: `POST /register` with validation (integration tests)
5. Then: session setup + auto-login after registration
6. Each step committed when green

This gives us a clear incremental path within the larger task.

**Can we reach consensus on this?** If anyone has objections or wants changes, speak now. Otherwise, I'll tell the team lead this is our agreed breakdown.
</teammate-message>

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user asked to "Spin up the team and complete the project" — a web-based multi-user todo list application. The project uses a 9-person ensemble team practicing mob/ensemble programming, with the coordinator agent (me) acting strictly as a facilitator who delegates work to teammates, relays questions to the project owner, and does NOT write code or make technical decisions.

   Key user directives throughout the conversation:

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - **Rust (nightly)** backend with Axum 0.8 web framework
   - **HTMX** for server-driven interactivity (HTML over the wire, progressive enhancement)
   - **Askama 0.14** for server-rendered HTML templates (askama_axum deprecated, merged into askama)
   - **PostgreSQL 16** with SQLx 0.8 (compile-time checked queries)
   - **Session-based auth** with Argon2 0.5, tower-sessions 0.14 + PostgresStore
   - **Tracing** + tracing-subscriber for structured logging
   - **tower-http** for static file serving (ServeDir) and middleware
   - **Docker Compose** for PostgreSQL in development

Here are some rules the team could adopt (to be added to `TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md`):

- **Commit on every green step**: After every Red-Green-Refactor cycle where tests pass, immediately `git add` the relevant files, commit, and push. No exceptions.
- **CI must be green before starting the next task**: Don't begin work on the next task until the previous task's commit has passed CI. Check `gh run list` after pushing.
- **No uncommitted work across task boundaries**: A task is not "complete" until its code is committed, pushed, and CI passes. Task status should not be updated to "completed" until this is verified.
- **One commit per TDD cycle maximum**: If you can't describe what changed in a sentence, you've done too much without committing.
- **Push immediately after commit**: Don't accumulate local commits — push after every commit so CI runs and the team can verify.

<teammate-message teammate_id="scott-wlaschin" color="purple" summary="Domain review complete, password hashing purity issue found">
I've completed my review of the current codebase after the context reset. Here's where things stand from a domain architecture perspective:

**What's good:**
- `ValidatedEmail` in `src/domain/email.rs` follows parse-don't-validate, normalizes to lowercase (US-2), has solid test coverage (10 tests)
- `UserId` and `User` in `src/domain/user.rs` use proper newtypes
- `Password` validation in `src/domain/password.rs` correctly validates min/max length
- All 16 unit tests pass

**Domain purity issue to address in Task #5:**
The `Password::hash()` method in `src/domain/password.rs` (line 28-35) calls `SaltString::generate(&mut rand::rng())` and `Argon2::default().hash_password()` -- this is I/O (random number generation + CPU-intensive hashing) inside the domain layer. Per our Type Design Principles #4 (pure domain core) and TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md Section 5.3 ("Domain logic is pure functions and types with no I/O"), hashing should be in the infrastructure layer.

**Proposed refactoring for Task #5:**
- `Password` (domain): validates length/emptiness only. Pure. Exposes `as_str()` or `as_bytes()` for the infrastructure layer to consume.
- Move `Password::hash()` and `PasswordHash_::verify()` to `src/infrastructure/` (e.g., `password_hasher.rs`). These are infrastructure concerns that interact with the Argon2 library and RNG.
- The service layer orchestrates: takes validated `Password`, passes to infrastructure for hashing, stores the hash.

This keeps the domain pure and testable without mocks. The domain tests for `Password` don't need to import argon2 at all.

**Ready to guide Task #5** (User registration with session infrastructure). The domain types are mostly in place -- we need the registration service, user repository, routes, templates, and session infrastructure. I'll guide TDD for the domain pieces and review all code for purity.
</teammate-message>

## 2026-02-08 20:51 UTC -- Assistant

Now I have the full picture. The team agreements are thorough in general but don't have explicit rules about the specific discipline problems that keep recurring. Here's what I'd recommend the team adopt:

---

The team's existing agreements are well-written but have gaps around the exact behaviors that keep causing problems. Here are rules the team could add to `TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md`:

### 1. **Commit Cadence Rule**
> Every TDD green step results in an immediate `git add` + `git commit` + `git push`. No accumulating uncommitted work. If you can't describe the change in one sentence, you've done too much since the last commit.

The current agreements say "TDD: Red-Green-Refactor" but never say *when to commit*. This is the root cause — it's implied but never stated.

### 2. **CI Gate Rule**
> No new work begins until the previous commit's CI run passes. After pushing, run `gh run list --limit 1` and verify the run completes green before writing new code. If CI fails, fixing it is the immediate priority — not starting the next feature.

The agreements say "Every commit must pass" the quality gates (Section 3, CI/CD Quality Gates) but don't say the team must *wait and verify*.

### 3. **Task Completion Rule**
> A task's status is only changed to "completed" after: (a) all code is committed, (b) the commit is pushed to origin, and (c) CI passes on that commit. Marking a task done while code is unstaged/uncommitted is not allowed.

The Definition of Done (Section 2) says "deployable -- not just merged, but shippable" but doesn't tie this to the task tracking workflow.

### 4. **Clean Working Tree Rule**
> The working tree should be clean (no uncommitted changes) at every task boundary. Before starting a new task, run `git status` and confirm there are no leftover uncommitted files from the previous task.

### 5. **No Red-State Abandonment Rule**
> Never leave code in a red (non-compiling or tests-failing) state in the working tree and switch to other work. If you're mid-red-step and need to switch tasks, either complete the green step and commit, or `git stash` the in-progress work.

---

These five rules directly address every discipline issue that has come up:
- Original Luca never committing (rules 1, 3)
- Task 4 marked done without committing (rule 3)
- CI failure ignored while starting Task 5 (rule 2)
- Broken uncommitted code sitting in working tree (rules 4, 5)

Want me to have the team discuss and adopt these rules? I'd broadcast the proposal and have them reach consensus, then update `TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md`.

---

## 2026-02-08 20:52 UTC -- User

<teammate-message teammate_id="kent-beck" color="yellow" summary="Full TDD review: 20 tests pass, code quality solid, next step is POST /register">
Kent Beck here with a detailed TDD review of the current uncommitted work. **All quality gates pass: 20 tests (16 unit + 4 integration), fmt clean, clippy clean.**

## What's Been Built (Uncommitted)

The team has made excellent progress on Task 5. Here's my assessment:

### Integration Test: GET /register (tests/api/register.rs)
**This is proper outside-in TDD.** The test checks:
- 200 status with text/html content type
- Page heading "Create account" and descriptive title
- Labeled form fields (email, password, password_confirmation)
- `autocomplete="new-password"` on password fields
- Submit button says "Create account" (action words)
- Link to /login ("Sign in")
- No error states on initial load (no aria-invalid, no error classes)

This test is driving the template and route. Good.

### Domain Types (src/domain/)
**Well test-driven.** 16 unit tests cover:
- `ValidatedEmail::parse()` -- empty, whitespace, missing @, missing domain dot, too long, trimming, case normalization, plus-tag support
- `Password::parse()` -- empty, too short (< 8), too long (> 128), exact boundary
- `Password::hash()` + `PasswordHash_::verify()` -- roundtrip verification

The types follow "parse, don't validate" correctly. `Password::hash()` consumes self, preventing plaintext reuse. `PasswordHash_` is a separate type -- you can't accidentally pass a raw password where a hash is expected.

### Registration Service (src/services/registration.rs)
**Good structure, good tracing instrumentation.** The `register_user` function:
- Validates email first (fail fast)
- Checks password confirmation match
- Validates password
- Hashes password (consuming the plaintext)
- Generates a UserId
- Inserts via repository
- Maps unique constraint violation (23505) to DuplicateEmail error
- Uses `#[tracing::instrument]` with proper skip/fields

**One TDD concern**: This service layer doesn't have its own unit tests yet. The `register_user` function takes a `PgPool` directly, which means you can't unit test it without a database. This is acceptable for now per our "no mocks for database" agreement, but it means this code path needs integration tests to cover it -- which leads to my next point.

### What's Missing (Next TDD Steps)

The `GET /register` route is tested and green. But there are **no integration tests for `POST /register`** yet. The service, repository, and migration exist but aren't exercised by any test. This is the critical next step:

1. **`POST /register` happy path**: Send valid email + password + confirmation, expect 303 redirect (to where? We need the session infrastructure)
2. **`POST /register` validation errors**: Missing email, short password, mismatched confirmation -- expect 422 with error messages in HTML
3. **`POST /register` duplicate email**: Register twice with same email -- expect the generic error message (account enumeration prevention)

The route handler for `POST /register` doesn't exist yet -- just `get_register`. That's the correct next failing test to write.

### Template (templates/register.html)
**Excellent accessibility.** Every input has a visible `<label>`, `aria-describedby` links errors to inputs, `aria-invalid` only appears when there's an error, the general error uses `role="alert"`, and the form works without JavaScript (standard `method="post" action="/register"`). This meets Heydon's requirements precisely.

### Startup Changes (src/startup.rs)
**Important addition**: `sqlx::migrate!("./migrations").run(&pool).await?` was added to `Application::build()`. This means migrations run automatically on startup, including in tests. Good for integration tests, but worth noting: this means every `spawn_app()` call applies migrations to the random test database automatically.

### Summary
The code is green, well-structured, and follows our agreements. The immediate priority is:
1. **Commit this work now** (it's green, don't risk losing it again)
2. Write failing integration test for `POST /register` with valid data
3. Implement the POST handler, connecting to the registration service
4. Commit at green
5. Then error cases: validation errors (422), duplicate email

This is solid work. The TDD discipline is much better than the pre-commit-loss version -- domain types were test-driven, and the GET route was driven by an integration test.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="carson-gross" color="orange">

<teammate-message teammate_id="heydon-pickering" color="cyan" summary="3 commits unpushed, code RED, one-line fix needed">
Current state:

**3 commits ahead of origin** (not pushed):
- `9af4522` Add HTMX indicator CSS and aria-atomic to live region
- `13e8dc5` Add registration page template, auth form CSS, and route
- `79db2c3` Add SQLx offline mode, query cache, and registration integration tests

**3 modified files not staged**: `src/routes/mod.rs`, `src/routes/register.rs`, `src/startup.rs`

**Build status: RED.** Compilation error in `src/routes/register.rs` line 51: `Redirect::see_other` doesn't exist in Axum 0.8. The available methods are `Redirect::to`, `Redirect::temporary`, and `Redirect::permanent`. For a POST redirect (303 See Other), `Redirect::to` is the correct replacement -- it returns a 303 in Axum 0.8.

This is a one-line fix. Someone needs to change `Redirect::see_other("/login")` to `Redirect::to("/login")` (or wherever the redirect should go -- note Steve Krug's requirement that registration redirects to the todo list, not the login page).

I've alerted Luca. The fix is trivial but nobody should push the 3 unpushed commits until the working tree is also green and committed.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="carson-gross" color="orange" summary="Carson's task breakdown recommendation for team consensus">
Team -- Carson here with my perspective on the task breakdown. This is a good time to reassess since we're mid-stream.

**What's already done (should stay as-is):**

- Task #4 (base HTML template + static file serving) is complete
- We're actively building the POST /register handler right now

**My recommendation for remaining tasks:**

The current breakdown (#5-#9, #20) maps roughly to the user stories, which is fine conceptually. But I think we should acknowledge the work already in progress and adjust:

**Task 5: Registration (US-1)** -- Currently in progress. Domain types (ValidatedEmail, Password, UserId), migration, infrastructure, service, and routes are being built right now. This is the right scope -- it proves the full stack works end-to-end.

**Task 6: Login + Logout + Session Infrastructure (US-2 + US-3)** -- These should stay bundled. Login and logout share session management. The session store (tower-sessions + PostgreSQL) is a cross-cutting concern that enables auth checking for all subsequent features. This task should include:
- Session middleware in the router
- Login GET/POST routes
- Logout POST route  
- Auth middleware/extractor for protected routes
- Session table migration

**Task 7: View Todo List + Add Todo (US-4 + US-5)** -- These are naturally coupled. The todo list page IS the add-todo form. You can't build one without the other. This is the core loop. Includes:
- TodoItem enum, TodoTitle, TodoItemId domain types
- Todos table migration
- Todo list GET route (with HX-Request header check for full page vs fragment)
- Add todo POST route
- Empty state design

**Tasks 8, 9, 20: Complete, Delete, Edit (US-6, US-7, US-8)** -- These are fine as separate tasks. They're independent HTMX interactions on the todo list. Each one is a clean TDD cycle: domain logic -> infrastructure -> route -> template partial.

**Missing cross-cutting concerns I see:**
1. **HTMX script inclusion** -- We haven't added the HTMX script tag to base.html yet. This should happen as part of Task 7 when we first need it.
2. **Auth guard middleware** -- Should be part of Task 6, applied to all routes after /login and /register.
3. **CSS auth-form component styles** -- Lea and Steve S should weigh in on when to add these. The form exists but has no component-layer CSS yet.

**Implementation order:** I agree with the walking skeleton order: Registration -> Login/Logout -> View+Add -> Complete -> Delete -> Edit. Each builds on the previous.

What does everyone else think? Kent, Scott, Marty -- does this granularity feel right?
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="scott-wlaschin" color="purple" summary="Consent on all five commit discipline rules">
**Position: Consent.** Full support for all five rules.

From a domain architecture perspective, these rules reinforce the type-safe pipeline approach. Each green step in TDD produces a valid, compiling program with a new proven property. That is exactly the right granularity for a commit -- it captures a provable increment of correctness. Accumulating uncommitted work is the antithesis of incremental proof.

A few observations on how these rules align with our existing principles:

**Rule 1 + Type-driven design**: Parse-don't-validate means each domain type's `parse()` function is a discrete, testable unit. Red-Green-Commit for `ValidatedEmail::parse()` is a natural commit boundary. If the commit message can't describe the change in one sentence ("Add ValidatedEmail with format validation"), the step was too big.

**Rule 3 + Definition of Done**: This closes the gap we had. Our Definition of Done in Section 2 lists quality gates but didn't explicitly require CI green before marking complete. This rule makes that explicit.

**Rule 5 + Pure domain core**: Red-state abandonment is how I/O leaks into the domain layer. Someone starts a refactor, gets interrupted, leaves half-moved code, and the next person works around it instead of finishing it. This rule prevents that structural drift.

No concerns, no alternatives needed. These are the right constraints. Consent to add to TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md as proposed.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="lea-verou" color="green" summary="Consent on all 5 commit discipline rules">
**Consent.** All five rules directly address problems I experienced firsthand:

- **Rule 1 (Commit on Every Green)**: I had CSS work that survived a repo reset only because I committed it. Uncommitted work from others was lost. This rule prevents that.

- **Rule 2 (CI Gate)**: We've been pushing commits and immediately starting new work without verifying CI. This led to cascading failures that were harder to diagnose later.

- **Rule 3 (Task Completion Requires CI Green)**: Tasks #4 and #5 were marked completed while code was still uncommitted locally. This created a false sense of progress.

- **Rule 4 (Clean Working Tree at Task Boundaries)**: I experienced confusion about which uncommitted files were mine vs. other team members' work-in-progress. My commit at `13e8dc5` accidentally included other team members' domain files because they were sitting in the working tree. Clean boundaries prevent this.

- **Rule 5 (No Red-State Abandonment)**: The `Redirect::see_other` compile error was left in the working tree while other work proceeded, causing test/build failures for anyone who tried to compile.

No concerns, no modifications needed. These are minimal, practical rules with clear enforcement criteria. Ship it.
</teammate-message>

**Local state is now clean and green**: working tree clean, up to date with origin, 12/12 tests passing locally.

- `Add auth-form hint style for field helper text` -- in progress (pushed while previous CI was still running)

<teammate-message teammate_id="heydon-pickering" color="cyan" summary="Task 5 has 4 a11y issues, not ready for completion">
Task #5 was marked completed but my accessibility review found 4 issues:

1. **Error elements conditionally rendered** -- should always be in DOM with `role="alert"` so `aria-describedby` always resolves and screen readers announce errors when they appear

<teammate-message teammate_id="kent-beck" color="yellow" summary="Consent: enthusiastic support for all 5 commit rules">
**Kent Beck: I consent enthusiastically.**

These five rules are the mechanical discipline that makes TDD actually work. I've been coaching these principles but we didn't have them codified, and the gaps showed. Specific observations:

**Rule 1 (Commit on Every Green Step)** -- This is the heart of it. The one-sentence test is a great heuristic. If you can't describe it in one sentence, you skipped a green step.

**Rule 2 (CI Gate)** -- This prevents the cascading problem we saw where broken commits piled up. Fix the build before writing new code -- always.

**Rule 3 (Task Completion Requires CI Green)** -- This closes the gap where Task 5 was marked complete while code was still uncommitted. "Done" means done, not "the code exists somewhere on disk."

**Rule 4 (Clean Working Tree at Task Boundaries)** -- Good hygiene. Prevents the confusion we had with leftover files from previous work muddying the picture.

**Rule 5 (No Red-State Abandonment)** -- The `git stash` escape hatch is the right answer. Never leave broken code lying around.

No concerns, no amendments. These rules codify what disciplined TDD practice already demands. Ready to add them to TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md as soon as consensus is reached.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="marty-cagan" color="blue" summary="CI red: SQLx cache missing + login code doesn't compile">
Coordinator, CI is still failing and the codebase is in a red state. Two separate issues:

**Issue 1: SQLx offline cache missing test queries.**
The `sqlx::query!` macro in `tests/api/register.rs:123` doesn't have a cached entry in `.sqlx/`. The `cargo sqlx prepare` command needs to be run with `-- --tests` to include test file queries. This has been the CI failure for the last 3 pushes.

**Issue 2: Login/logout code doesn't compile.**
Someone committed login/logout code (Task #6) that doesn't compile:
- `src/routes/login.rs:32` uses `#[axum::debug_handler]` but the `macros` feature isn't enabled in Cargo.toml
- `post_login` and `post_logout` handlers don't satisfy Axum's `Handler` trait (likely a `Session` extractor issue)
- This code was committed and pushed while in a red state -- violating Rule 5 (No Red-State Abandonment)

The code compiles and tests pass when building without `--tests` because the login code exists but the broken handlers are only referenced in `startup.rs` (which does compile for the lib target). But `cargo sqlx prepare -- --tests` fails because the test crate pulls in the broken handlers.

**What needs to happen:**
1. Fix the login/logout compilation errors (Luca's Task #6 work)
2. Run `cargo sqlx prepare -- --tests` to update the query cache
3. Verify all tests pass locally with `SQLX_OFFLINE=true`
4. Commit and push
5. Verify CI passes

Per the new commit discipline rules: no new work until CI is green. This is the immediate priority.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="scott-wlaschin" color="purple" summary="Fixed tower-sessions version, all pushed, CI queued">
Done. All code committed and pushed.

**What was fixed:**
The committed login/logout code (`199694a`) used `tower-sessions = "0.13"` which depends on `axum-core 0.4`. Our `axum 0.8` uses `axum-core 0.5`. This caused the `Session` extractor to fail the `Handler` trait bound -- the code would not compile.

- `cargo clippy -- -D warnings` -- clean

<teammate-message teammate_id="marty-cagan" color="blue" summary="All 4 a11y issues are US-1 acceptance criteria violations">
Marty here. Confirmed -- all four issues Heydon flagged are acceptance criteria from US-1:

1. **Error elements in DOM with `aria-describedby`** -- US-1 line 42: "Validation errors are associated with inputs via `aria-describedby`". The error elements must be in the DOM for `aria-describedby` to reference valid IDs.

2. **Password hint** -- supports line 34: "Password must be at least 8 characters". Telling the user the requirement *before* they fail is better UX than making them guess and showing an error.

3. **Remove `minlength`** -- browser-native validation fights our custom inline error pattern. Users would get inconsistent error experiences.

4. **Redirect to todo list** -- US-1 line 31: "Successful registration creates a new user account and redirects to the todo list (user is automatically logged in)." Redirecting to `/login` instead violates this directly.

Task #5 cannot be marked complete until these are fixed. The Definition of Done says "All acceptance criteria from the user story are met." These four are not met yet. Correct to block.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="lea-verou" color="green" summary="CONSENT on all 5 commit discipline rules">
**Vote on commit discipline rules: CONSENT on all 5.**

1. **Commit on every green step** -- CONSENT. Small, frequent commits make it easy to bisect issues and reduce merge pain. This session has been a masterclass in what happens when commits pile up.

2. **CI gate before new work** -- CONSENT. We just experienced exactly why this matters. Four requests to push before it happened. A hard gate prevents this.

3. **Task completion requires CI green** -- CONSENT. A task that passes locally but fails CI is not done. This is just intellectual honesty.

4. **Clean working tree at task boundaries** -- CONSENT. Uncommitted changes from one task bleeding into the next is how we ended up with domain files in my CSS commit. Clean boundaries prevent cross-contamination.

5. **No red-state abandonment** -- CONSENT. Leaving the codebase red is leaving a trap for the next person. Fix it or revert it.

No concerns, no blocks. These rules codify what we should have been doing all along. Standing by for CI results -- not touching any files.
</teammate-message>

I'm ready to work on Task #7 (View todo list + Add todo item, US-4 + US-5). From a domain architecture perspective, the types we need are:

1. **TodoTitle** -- parse-don't-validate newtype (max 300 chars per glossary, trim whitespace, reject empty/whitespace-only)
2. **TodoItem** -- enum state machine: `Pending { id, user_id, title, created_at }` and `Completed { id, user_id, title, created_at, completed_at }` 
3. **TodoItemId** -- newtype wrapping Uuid

The `completed_at` column in the DB serves as the discriminator (NULL = Pending, present = Completed).

For the service layer: `add_todo(pool, user_id, title_string) -> Result<TodoItem, AddTodoError>` and `get_todos(pool, user_id) -> Result<Vec<TodoItem>>`.

I'll start writing the domain types with TDD. Should I proceed?
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="heydon-pickering" color="cyan" summary="Login a11y review: mostly passes, one minor inconsistency">
Quick accessibility review of the login template (Task #6) -- mostly good, one minor issue:

**Passes:**
- Visible labels for both fields
- `autocomplete="email"` and `autocomplete="current-password"` (correct for login)
- "Sign in" action button label
- Generic error: "That email or password didn't work. Try again." (no credential leakage)
- `role="alert"` on error div
- Email repopulated on error
- Session cycling on login (session fixation prevention)
- Logout flushes session
- Link to registration page

**Minor issue -- no `aria-live` region for the error announcement:**
The login error div (line 9) uses `role="alert"` which is correct -- but it's conditionally rendered (only when `error_message` is `Some`). Same pattern we just fixed in registration. When the error div pops into existence, `role="alert"` should cause the announcement. However, the more robust pattern (same as registration) would be to always have the error div in the DOM, empty when no error. This isn't as critical for login since there are no field-level errors, but it's inconsistent with the pattern we just established in registration.

**Missing from US-2 acceptance criteria:**
- "Forgot password?" link is not present. US-2 says: "For MVP, it leads to a placeholder page explaining the feature is coming soon." This is a product requirement, not accessibility. Flagging for Marty.

This is not blocking -- login is functional and accessible. The conditional error div is a minor inconsistency that could be addressed as a quick follow-up. The "Forgot password?" link is a product gap.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="kent-beck" color="yellow" summary="Task 7 status: domain types ready, TDD guidance for next steps">
Status update on Task 7 (View todo list and add todo item):

**TDD observation:**
The domain types are well-built with good unit tests, but we're building bottom-up. The outside-in TDD approach would start with a failing integration test for GET /todos and POST /todos, then build inward. The domain types can be committed as a foundation step though, since they're independently tested and don't break compilation.

**Recommended next steps:**
1. Commit the domain types (todo_title.rs, todo_item.rs) with their unit tests - they compile independently and have passing tests
2. Apply the migration (already applied to local DB, needs `.sqlx` cache update after wiring queries)
3. Write a failing integration test: `GET /todos` when not logged in should redirect to `/login`
4. Build outward from there: auth extractor, route handler, template, service, repository

**Important note:** I regenerated the `.sqlx` offline cache to include the new queries, but since the route/service/repo files were removed, the cache may need updating again when they're re-added. The `chrono` feature is enabled on SQLx so TIMESTAMPTZ maps correctly to `chrono::DateTime<Utc>`.

Standing by to coach the TDD cycle and help fix issues as the team builds this out.

<teammate-message teammate_id="marty-cagan" color="blue" summary="Task 7 discovery brief: US-4 + US-5 criteria">
**Task #7 Discovery Brief -- US-4 (View Todo List) + US-5 (Add Todo Item)**

This is the core user loop. After this task, we have a usable product. Here's what matters from a product perspective:

---

**US-4: View Todo List -- Key Acceptance Criteria**

1. Todo list is the main screen after login (redirect from `/` or after auth)
2. Clear `<h1>` heading (e.g., "My Todos")
3. Items in a semantic list (`<ul>` or `<ol>`) -- screen readers announce item count automatically
4. Each item shows title and completion status
5. Completed items visually distinct (strikethrough + secondary indicator, not just color)
6. **Empty state**: "No todos yet." -- brief and friendly, not a blank screen. The add input above makes the next action obvious.
7. Page title: "My Todos -- Todo List"
8. Proper landmarks: `<main>`, `<nav>`, `<header>`, skip link as first focusable element
9. Authorization: each user sees ONLY their own todos
10. Works without JavaScript

**US-5: Add Todo Item -- Key Acceptance Criteria**

1. Input at top of list, prominently placed, with visible `<label>` ("New todo") and placeholder ("What do you need to do?")
2. New items are `Pending` state
3. After adding: input cleared, focus returns to input (ready for next item)
4. **Empty/whitespace submissions silently ignored** -- no error message (accidental Enter is not intentional)
5. Max 300 characters -- inline validation error if exceeded
6. Works without JS (full page reload, item appears in list)
7. HTMX: item appended without reload
8. `aria-live` region announces "Todo added" after HTMX swap
9. Logged with structured tracing

**Domain Model (from glossary)**
- `TodoItem` enum: `Pending` / `Completed` (with timestamps)
- `TodoTitle`: validated string, max 300 chars, trimmed, non-empty
- `TodoItemId(Uuid)`

**Success Metrics**
- US-4: User sees their entire list within 1 second of logging in
- US-5: Adding a todo takes fewer than 5 seconds from thought to captured item

**Edge Cases to Keep in Mind**
- Zero todos (empty state), one todo, many todos (100+)
- Special characters, HTML entities, emoji in titles
- Titles at exactly 300 chars vs 301 chars
- Whitespace-only input (silently ignored)
- Rapid successive additions (no duplicates)

The untracked domain files (`todo_item.rs`, `todo_title.rs`) align with the agreed model. The mob should verify they match through proper TDD and commit incrementally.

Let's build the core loop.
</teammate-message>

The code follows our domain principles well:
- **TodoTitle**: Parse-don't-validate, 300 char max, trims, 7 unit tests. Clean.
- **TodoItem**: Enum state machine (Pending/Completed). Makes illegal states unrepresentable. 2 unit tests.
- **TodoItemId**: Newtype wrapping Uuid. Good.
- **TodoRecord**: Infrastructure-layer record with `to_domain()` conversion. Uses `completed_at` as discriminator. Correct.

- **AuthenticatedUser extractor**: Clean Axum extractor, redirects unauthenticated users to /login. No `#[async_trait]` needed in Axum 0.8.
- **todos route**: Proper error-to-user-copy translation for `TooLong`, silently ignores empty submissions per US-5.
- **SQLx type overrides**: Uses `as "completed_at: DateTime<Utc>"` to force chrono types. Correct approach.

**Minor notes for future refactoring (NOT blocking):**
1. `TodoItem::new_pending()` calls `Utc::now()` and `TodoItemId::new()` -- these are I/O in the domain. Same pattern as `Password::hash()`. Non-blocking but makes unit testing non-deterministic.
2. `TodoRecord::to_domain()` uses `.expect()` on `TodoTitle::parse()` -- trusting DB data. Acceptable for now but a soft invariant.

**What's needed for Task #7 integration tests:**
- Tests for GET /todos (authenticated/unauthenticated)
- Tests for POST /todos (add item, empty submission ignored, title too long)
- Tests for todo list display (items appear in list, empty state)

<teammate-message teammate_id="heydon-pickering" color="cyan" summary="Task 7 a11y review: 1 fix needed (error div pattern)">
**Task #7 Accessibility Review -- mostly passes, 1 issue to fix:**

**Passes:**
- `<h1>My Todos</h1>` and `<title>My Todos -- Todo List</title>` -- correct
- Visible `<label for="title">New todo</label>` with placeholder -- per US-5
- `<ul class="todo-list" role="list">` -- correct Safari VoiceOver fix
- Empty state: `<p>No todos yet.</p>` -- simple, correct
- Logout as `<form>` with `<button>` in nav -- correct for state-changing action
- `maxlength="300"` on input -- correct
- `autocomplete="off"` -- correct (todo titles aren't reusable form data)
- Auth-protected routes via `AuthenticatedUser` extractor -- correct
- Empty/whitespace submissions silently redirect (303) -- matches US-5.4
- User isolation (users can't see each other's todos) -- tested

**Issue: Error div conditionally rendered (lines 30-34)**
Same pattern we fixed twice already. Should be:
```html
<div class="todo-add__error" role="alert">{% if let Some(error) = error_message %}{{ error }}{% endif %}</div>
```

This is a one-line fix. The error div should always be in the DOM with `role="alert"`, empty when no error.

**Not blocking but noted for future tasks:**
- Todo items currently just display a span with the title. The checkbox toggle (Task #8), delete button (Task #9), and edit button (Task #20) will add interactive elements. The `<li>` structure will need to evolve.
- HTMX enhancement (item append without reload, status announcer, focus return) is not yet present. This is expected -- no-JS baseline first.

Overall this is solid. One quick fix needed, then Task #7 meets the accessibility DoD.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="scott-wlaschin" color="purple" summary="Task 8 domain review CONSENT, fixed Axum path syntax">
Task #8 (Complete a todo item) status update. All quality gates pass (fmt, clippy, 58 tests green).

**Critical fix I made:**
- Fixed Axum 0.8 path parameter syntax in `startup.rs`: changed `/todos/:id/toggle` to `/todos/{id}/toggle`. Axum 0.8 uses `{param}` not `:param`. This caused ALL 28 integration tests to fail (panic on router construction).

**Domain review of Task #8 code -- CONSENT:**

1. **`TodoItem::complete(self) -> Self`** -- Clean state transition, takes ownership, Pending -> Completed with `Utc::now()`. No-op if already completed. Follows state machine in glossary.

2. **`TodoItem::uncomplete(self) -> Self`** -- Reverse transition, Completed -> Pending. Drops `completed_at`. No-op if already pending. Matches US-6 toggle requirement.

3. **`toggle_todo_completion()` service** -- Looks up todo by ID, verifies ownership (user_id match), toggles state, persists. Clean error types: `NotFound`, `Unauthorized`, `Unexpected`.

4. **`find_todo_by_id()` / `update_todo_completion()` repository** -- Uses same chrono type override pattern as existing queries. `fetch_optional` for find, `UPDATE SET completed_at` for toggle.

5. **Template** -- Checkbox toggle as `<form>` with `<button>`, accessible `aria-label` with todo title context. Unicode ballot box characters (U+2610 / U+2611) for visual state. Works without JS.

6. **5 new domain unit tests** for complete/uncomplete transitions.

**One test-suite note:** There's a test helper `extract_todo_id` in `tests/api/todos.rs` that's unused (gives a compiler warning). It's likely for the upcoming toggle integration tests. Not blocking but should be used or removed before commit.

**Needs before commit:**
- Integration tests for toggle (POST /todos/{id}/toggle)
- The `extract_todo_id` helper should be connected to tests
- Verify the `#[allow(dead_code)]` on `TodoItemView::id` can now be removed since `id` is used in the template

Let me know if I should help with any of these.

Task #8 (Complete a Todo Item, US-6) is complete. Here's the summary:

**What was built:**

**Domain layer:**
- `TodoItem::complete()` -- transitions Pending to Completed (no-op if already completed)

<teammate-message teammate_id="heydon-pickering" color="cyan" summary="Task 8 a11y issue: button must be native checkbox">
Task #8 was marked complete but there's an accessibility issue: the todo toggle is implemented as a `<button>` with Unicode checkbox characters instead of a native `<input type="checkbox">`.

Screen readers announce "Mark Buy groceries as complete, button" instead of "Buy groceries, checkbox, not checked." This is wrong semantics -- users universally expect checkbox behavior for toggle states in lists.

I've sent Carson the correct pattern: native `<input type="checkbox">` with a `<label>` that IS the todo title. This gives us:
- Correct checkbox semantics and state announcement
- Native `aria-checked` for free (no manual ARIA)
- Larger click target (clicking the title toggles the checkbox)
- Cleaner HTML (no Unicode characters, no `aria-label`)

This needs to be fixed before Task #8 is truly complete. Also: the error div on the todos page (lines 30-34) is still conditionally rendered -- same issue I flagged earlier. Two fixes needed.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="heydon-pickering" color="cyan">
{"type":"idle_notification","from":"heydon-pickering","timestamp":"2026-02-08T21:15:22.344Z","idleReason":"available","summary":"[to carson-gross] Toggle must be native checkbox, not button - a11y requirement"}
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="scott-wlaschin" color="purple" summary="Task 8 all green, 64 tests pass, ready to commit">
All quality gates GREEN for Task #8 complete/uncomplete:
- fmt: pass

- 64 tests pass: 30 unit + 34 integration

Task #8 integration test coverage (6 new tests):
1. `post_toggle_completes_a_pending_todo` -- happy path
2. `post_toggle_uncompletes_a_completed_todo` -- double toggle
3. `post_toggle_returns_404_for_nonexistent_todo` -- error case
4. `post_toggle_returns_403_for_another_users_todo` -- authorization
5. `post_toggle_redirects_to_login_when_unauthenticated` -- auth guard
6. `toggle_button_has_accessible_label` -- a11y

Ready to commit and push Task #8, then move to Task #9 (Delete). The uncommitted changes span 8 files across domain, infrastructure, service, route, template, and test layers.

Task #9 (Delete a todo item) status update. All quality gates GREEN (fmt, clippy, 64 tests).

**Changes I made for Task #9:**
1. Wired up delete route: `.route("/todos/{id}/delete", axum::routing::post(post_delete_todo))` in startup.rs (using Axum 0.8 `{id}` syntax)
2. Added delete button to template: `<form method="post" action="/todos/{{ todo.id }}/delete">` with `<button aria-label="Delete &quot;{{ todo.title }}&quot;">` -- per US-7 (button not link for destructive action, accessible label)

4. Updated glossary with `DeleteTodoError` variants and `delete_todo()` service description

**Domain review of Task #9 code -- CONSENT:**

1. **`delete_todo()` service** -- Correct pattern: find by ID, verify ownership (user_id match), then delete. Same error pattern as toggle: `NotFound`, `Unauthorized`, `Unexpected`.

2. **`delete_todo()` repository** -- Simple `DELETE FROM todos WHERE id = $1`. Clean.

3. **`post_delete_todo` route** -- Same structure as toggle route: Path<Uuid> extractor, ownership check via service, 404/403 error responses, redirect to /todos on success.

4. **Template delete button** -- Uses multiplication sign character (U+2715) for the X icon. Has `aria-label` with todo title. Works without JS (form POST).

**What still needs doing for Task #9:**
- Integration tests for delete (POST /todos/{id}/delete)
- Per US-7: confirmation mechanism before deletion ("keep it lightweight, not a modal dialog") -- this could be a JS enhancement or a simple confirm/cancel toggle
- After deletion, focus management (focus to next item or to add input)

The integration test suite for delete should mirror the toggle tests: happy path delete, delete nonexistent (404), delete another user's todo (403), unauthenticated delete (redirect), delete last item transitions to empty state, and verify the delete button has an accessible label.

<teammate-message teammate_id="scott-wlaschin" color="purple" summary="Domain review for Tasks #9 and #20 with CONSENT">
**Domain Architecture Review -- Task #9 (Delete) and Task #20 (Edit) -- CONSENT**

Both features pass domain review. Here is what I did and found:

## Task #9 (Delete) -- Complete
The 5 delete integration tests are solid and cover all the cases I recommended: happy path with empty-state transition, 404 for nonexistent, 403 for unauthorized, unauthenticated redirect, and accessible aria-label. No domain concerns.

## Task #20 (Edit) -- In Progress, Route Wired

**What I did:**
1. **Wired up the edit route** in `startup.rs` (lines 66-69): `/todos/{id}/edit` with GET (form) + POST (submit). The imports and route handlers were already in `routes/mod.rs` and `routes/todos.rs`, but the route was not registered in the router.
2. **Added edit link** to `templates/todos.html` (lines 49-52): Each todo now has a pencil icon (&#x270E;) link with `aria-label="Edit &quot;{{ todo.title }}&quot;"` for accessibility.
3. **Updated glossary** (`docs/glossary.md`):
   - Fixed `edit_todo_title()` -> `update_todo_title()` to match actual function name
   - Added `UpdateTitleError` variants (NotFound, Unauthorized, InvalidTitle) to error table
   - Added context-specific error copy: `TodoTitleError::Empty` in edit context maps to "Title cannot be empty" (vs silently ignored in add context per US-5)
   - Updated state machine reference

**Domain observations:**
- `update_todo_title` service correctly follows the ownership-check + parse-don't-validate pattern
- `UpdateTitleError` enum has proper variants matching the existing error convention
- The `get_edit_todo` handler reaches directly into `todo_repository::find_todo_by_id` instead of going through a service function -- minor architectural concern for MVP, noting for future cleanup
- Error copy differentiation between add (silent ignore) and edit ("Title cannot be empty") is correct -- editing is an intentional action where empty titles should be rejected

**Quality gate: 69 tests green (30 unit + 39 integration), clippy clean, fmt clean.**

Edit integration tests are still needed. I recommend the same pattern as delete: happy path edit, 404, 403, unauthenticated redirect, empty title validation (422), too-long title validation (422), and edit form displays current title.
