<teammate-message teammate_id="luca-palmieri" color="blue" summary="Infrastructure assessment and proposed remaining task breakdown">
Thanks for the heads-up. I have reviewed the user stories, PROJECT.md, TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md, and the current codebase state. Here is my assessment from the infrastructure and Rust engineering perspective.

**Current state**: All MVP user stories (US-1 through US-8) have been implemented and have integration tests. We have 78 tests passing (30 unit + 48 integration), all quality gates green. The no-JS baseline works for every feature.

**What is NOT yet done per the acceptance criteria and Definition of Done**:

1. **HTMX progressive enhancement** -- Every user story has acceptance criteria for HTMX-enhanced interactions (partial updates, no full-page reload, inline validation). None of this has been built yet. This is a significant chunk of remaining work. Specifically:
   - US-1: HTMX inline validation on registration, no full-page reload
   - US-2: HTMX login without full-page reload
   - US-5: HTMX appends new todo without page reload, `aria-live` announcement
   - US-6: HTMX in-place toggle without page reload, `aria-live` announcement
   - US-7: HTMX removes item from DOM without reload, `aria-live` announcement, **confirmation before delete** (not implemented at all)
   - US-8: HTMX inline editing without page navigation

2. **Delete confirmation** (US-7) -- The acceptance criteria explicitly require "Confirmation mechanism before deletion" -- this is not implemented even at the no-JS baseline level.

3. **"Forgot password?" placeholder page** (US-2) -- Login page should have this link per AC.

4. **Focus management after HTMX swaps** -- The TEAM_AGREEMENTS define an HTMX Focus Management Protocol. This needs to be implemented alongside HTMX work.

5. **`aria-live` regions** -- Several stories require screen reader announcements for dynamic updates. These are partially missing even in the no-JS version.

6. **Password progressive enhancement** (US-1) -- The JS toggle that replaces the confirm field with a visibility toggle. This is TypeScript work.

7. **Cache control headers** (US-3) -- "After logout, the back button does not show authenticated content (no cache leaks)" -- needs `Cache-Control: no-store` on authenticated pages.

8. **Skip link** -- US-4 requires "Skip link to main content is the first focusable element." Need to verify this is in place.

9. **`sqlx-data.json` / offline mode** -- Per TEAM_AGREEMENTS, we should run `cargo sqlx prepare` and commit the offline query data for CI. Currently CI needs a live database for compile-time query checks.

**My proposed task breakdown for remaining work**:

| Task | Description | Dependencies |
|------|-------------|-------------|
| A | Delete confirmation mechanism (no-JS baseline) | None |
| B | Forgot password placeholder page | None |
| C | Cache-control headers for authenticated pages | None |
| D | Verify/fix skip link and landmark structure | None |
| E | aria-live regions for existing features (no-JS) | None |
| F | HTMX integration: todos (add, toggle, delete, edit) | A, E |
| G | HTMX integration: auth forms (register, login) | E |
| H | Password visibility toggle (TypeScript PE) | G |
| I | Focus management after HTMX swaps | F, G |
| J | sqlx-data.json for offline CI | None |

Tasks A-E and J are independent and could be parallelized. F-I depend on the earlier work.

The biggest open question for the mob: How do we want to approach the HTMX layer? Carson should lead that discussion since it touches his area of expertise. The server endpoint convention (same URL, check `HX-Request` header, return fragment vs full page) will touch every handler.

Ready to join the mob discussion whenever the team convenes.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="heydon-pickering" color="cyan" summary="Final comprehensive a11y review: 3 issues, mostly passes">
**Final Accessibility Review -- All MVP Features (Tasks #1-#9, #20)**

All tasks are marked complete. 48 tests passing, working tree clean, CI green. Here is my comprehensive accessibility assessment of the final codebase.

---

**PASSES (good work by the team):**

Base template (`base.html`):
- `<html lang="en">`, proper viewport meta, no zoom restriction
- Skip link with `.skip-link` class (primary blue on focus, `:focus-visible`)
- Landmark regions: `<header>`, `<main id="main-content">`, `<footer>`, `<nav aria-label="Main navigation">`
- `.page-layout` grid, CSS cascade layers
- Dynamic `<title>` block

Registration (`register.html`):
- Visible labels, `autocomplete` attributes, `novalidate`
- Error elements always in DOM with `role="alert"`
- `aria-describedby` always present, `aria-invalid` conditional
- Password hint "At least 8 characters" linked via `aria-describedby`
- Account enumeration prevention (generic error message)
- Email repopulated on error, passwords never repopulated

Login (`login.html`):
- Visible labels, `autocomplete="current-password"` (correct for login)
- Generic credential error (no leakage)
- Session cycling on login (session fixation prevention)

Todo list (`todos.html`):
- `<h1>My Todos</h1>`, descriptive `<title>`
- Visible label "New todo" on add input with placeholder
- `<ul role="list">` (Safari VoiceOver fix)
- Empty state "No todos yet."
- Auth-protected routes, user isolation
- Item-specific `aria-label` on edit and delete buttons
- Logout as form+button in nav

CSS (`main.css`):
- Motion-safe tokens (default 0s)
- `forced-colors` support
- Double-ring focus technique with 3:1+ contrast
- `.visually-hidden` and `.skip-link` utilities
- Contrast-safe color tokens with usage restriction comments

---

**REMAINING ISSUES (3 items):**

**1. Toggle is button, not native checkbox (todos.html lines 42-46)**
The completion toggle uses `<button>` with Unicode checkbox characters. Screen readers announce "button" semantics instead of "checkbox" semantics. Should be `<input type="checkbox">` with `<label>` as the title. I've sent the corrected pattern to Carson. This is the most significant remaining accessibility issue.

**2. Conditionally rendered error divs (todos.html lines 30-34, edit_todo.html lines 14-18, 32-34, login.html lines 8-12)**
Three templates still use the old pattern of conditionally rendering error elements. They should always be in the DOM with `role="alert"`, empty when no error. The registration template was fixed; these three were not.

**3. Edit page error uses conditional `aria-describedby` (edit_todo.html line 30)**
Same pattern: `aria-describedby` and error `<p>` only rendered when error exists. Should always be present. Also missing `role="alert"` on the error element (line 33).

---

**NOT BLOCKING but noted:**
- Delete has no confirmation step (US-7 requires "confirm before deleting"). The current delete button submits directly. Steve Schoger designed an inline confirm/cancel pattern that hasn't been implemented.
- No HTMX enhancements yet (all interactions are full page reloads). This is acceptable for MVP but the progressive enhancement layer is missing.
- No status announcer div in the base template for HTMX swap announcements (needed when HTMX is added).
- Login error div is conditionally rendered (minor inconsistency with registration pattern).
- "Forgot password?" placeholder link missing from login page (US-2 requirement).

---

**Summary:** The MVP is functional and mostly accessible. The checkbox semantics issue (#1) is the most important fix -- it affects every screen reader user's experience of the core feature. The conditional error div pattern (#2, #3) is a consistency issue that should be fixed to match the registration template. These are straightforward fixes that won't require new tests.

Overall assessment: the team has built a solid accessible foundation. The semantic HTML, landmark regions, label associations, and ARIA patterns are correct throughout. Good work.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="marty-cagan" color="blue" summary="MVP review: 7/8 pass, delete confirm gap, PE items outstanding">
**MVP Acceptance Review Complete**

All 10 feature tasks are marked completed. 48 tests green, CI green, working tree clean. I've reviewed every user story against the implementation. Here's the summary:

**7 of 8 user stories PASS the no-JS baseline.** US-7 (Delete) has one gap:

**US-7 Gap: No delete confirmation step.** The template at `todos.html:53-58` submits the delete form directly with no confirmation. US-7 acceptance criteria require: "Confirmation mechanism before deletion -- keep it lightweight, not a modal dialog." Lea already committed CSS for a `details/summary` confirmation pattern (`5bdf62e`), but the template hasn't adopted it. This is a safety feature -- users should not lose a todo with a single accidental click.

**Outstanding progressive enhancement items** (in acceptance criteria but not yet implemented):
1. HTMX enhancements for add, toggle, delete, edit (US-4 through US-8 all specify "HTMX enhances with no full-page reload")
2. `aria-live` announcements for dynamic updates ("Todo added", "Todo deleted", state change)
3. Password visibility toggle replacing confirm field (US-1 JS enhancement)

Analysis:
Let me chronologically analyze the entire conversation:

1. **Context Recovery**: This session is a continuation from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary provided details about a todo list web application project with a 9-person ensemble team.

2. **Initial State**: The user had previously asked to "Spin up the team and complete the project." The coordinator role (me) delegates to teammates, doesn't write code.

3. **User's question about team rules**: The user asked "what rules could the team put in place to clean up their behavior?" in response to recurring discipline issues (not committing, not pushing, skipping tasks ahead).

4. **I proposed 5 commit discipline rules**:
   - Rule 1: Commit on every green step
   - Rule 2: CI gate before new work
   - Rule 3: Task completion requires CI green
   - Rule 4: Clean working tree at task boundaries
   - Rule 5: No red-state abandonment

5. **User approved**: "Yes, go ahead and have the team adopt those rules. Also tell them to commit and push the current uncommitted work immediately"

6. **Broadcast and voting process**: I broadcast rules to all 9 teammates. Got consent from: Steve Krug, Heydon, Steve Schoger, Marty, Scott, Kent, Lea, Carson, Luca (eventually all 9/9).

7. **Persistent push problems**: Throughout the session, the team repeatedly failed to push commits despite multiple requests. This was the dominant issue:
   - Kent reviewed code instead of pushing (asked 3+ times)
   - Commits accumulated without being pushed
   - New code was written on top of unpushed commits
   - Code was committed at RED state (tests failing)

8. **Task 5 (Registration) a11y issues**: Heydon found 4 issues:
   - Error elements conditionally rendered (should always be in DOM with role="alert")
   - Password hint "At least 8 characters" missing
   - Remove minlength="8" attribute
   - Redirect to /login instead of /todos

9. **These were eventually fixed** in commit `6c757bc`.

    - Missing PostgreSQL service in CI (fixed earlier)
    - tower-sessions version incompatibility (0.13 vs 0.14 for Axum 0.8)
    - SQLx offline cache missing test queries
    - Login code not compiling (Redirect::see_other doesn't exist in Axum 0.8)

    - Tasks 1-4: Already done before this session
    - Task 5: Registration - completed with a11y fixes
    - Task 6: Login/Logout - completed
    - Task 7: View + Add todos - completed
    - Task 8: Complete/toggle todo - completed
    - Task 9: Delete todo - completed
    - Task 20: Edit todo title - completed

12. **Final state**: All MVP tasks complete, 48 integration tests passing, all CI green. Commit discipline rules added to TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md.

    - Toggle checkbox semantics (button vs native checkbox) - Heydon's feedback

- No other explicit user messages in this session

The MVP is complete. The user was informed. The question is whether to proceed with post-MVP tasks or shut down the team.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user's original request (from prior session) was to "Spin up the team and complete the project" — a web-based multi-user todo list application. In this session, the user asked: "what rules could the team put in place to clean up their behavior?" referring to recurring discipline issues (not committing, not pushing, accumulating uncommitted work, marking tasks complete prematurely, skipping ahead to future tasks). The user then approved adopting the proposed rules: "Yes, go ahead and have the team adopt those rules. Also tell them to commit and push the current uncommitted work immediately." The coordinator role (me) strictly delegates to teammates, does not write code or make technical decisions.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - **Rust (nightly)** backend with **Axum 0.8** web framework
   - **PostgreSQL 16** with **SQLx 0.8** (compile-time checked queries, offline mode with `.sqlx/` cache)
   - **Askama 0.13** for server-rendered HTML templates (no separate askama_axum crate)
   - **tower-sessions 0.14** + **tower-sessions-sqlx-store 0.15** (required for Axum 0.8 / axum-core 0.5 compatibility)
   - **Argon2** password hashing with `Password::hash()` consuming self to prevent plaintext reuse
   - **Parse-don't-validate** pattern for domain types (ValidatedEmail, Password, TodoTitle, TodoItem enum)
   - **TDD (Red-Green-Refactor)** — strict Kent Beck style, outside-in
   - **Progressive enhancement**: HTML works without JavaScript, HTMX enhances (not yet implemented)
   - **WCAG 2.2 AA** accessibility: semantic HTML, aria-describedby, role="alert", visible labels
   - **CI/CD**: GitHub Actions with PostgreSQL service, cargo fmt + clippy + test pipeline
   - **Axum 0.8 specifics**: `Redirect::to()` is 303 See Other (not `see_other()`), path params use `{id}` not `:id`
   - **Askama HTML entity encoding**: uses `&#39;` not `&#x27;` for apostrophes
   - **CSS cascade layers**: @layer reset, tokens, base, layout, components, utilities with oklch colors
   - **5 Commit Discipline Rules** adopted by team consensus (9/9):
     1. Commit on every green step + push immediately
     2. CI gate — no new work until CI passes
     3. Task completion requires CI green
     4. Clean working tree at task boundaries
     5. No red-state abandonment

3. Files and Code Sections:
   - **TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md** — Team conventions, Definition of Done, code conventions, architectural principles. Commit discipline rules were added as Section 3 subsection by Kent (commit `619a7d0`).
   - **docs/user-stories.md** — 8 user stories (US-1 through US-8) with acceptance criteria, edge cases, success metrics. Created by Marty.
   - **PROJECT.md** — Project owner constraints: tech stack, development mandates (TDD, mob programming, consensus, quality gates), MVP scope.
   - **CLAUDE.md** — Coordinator agent instructions: strict delegation mode, team roster with 9 members and profiles.
   - **.github/workflows/ci.yml** — CI pipeline with PostgreSQL service, cargo fmt/clippy/test. Updated to include `DATABASE_URL` for SQLx compile-time checks.
   - **flake.nix** — Nix dev environment with rust-overlay, pkg-config, openssl, sqlx-cli, docker-compose.
   - **templates/register.html** — Registration form with always-in-DOM error elements (`role="alert"`), password hint, `aria-describedby`, `aria-invalid` conditional. Fixed in commit `6c757bc`.
   - **templates/todos.html** — Todo list with semantic `<ul role="list">`, empty state, add form with label/placeholder, toggle/delete/edit buttons. Error div pattern still conditionally rendered (outstanding a11y issue).
   - **templates/edit_todo.html** — Edit todo form (created for Task 20). Has conditional error rendering (outstanding a11y issue).
   - **src/routes/register.rs** — GET/POST /register handlers. Redirect changed from `/login` to `/todos` per US-1. `Redirect::to()` used (not `see_other()`).
   - **src/routes/todos.rs** — GET/POST /todos, POST /todos/{id}/toggle, POST /todos/{id}/delete, GET/POST /todos/{id}/edit handlers.
   - **src/routes/auth.rs** — `AuthenticatedUser` extractor that pulls user_id from session, redirects to /login if not authenticated.
   - **src/domain/email.rs** — `ValidatedEmail::parse()` with format validation, normalization (lowercase, trim).
   - **src/domain/password.rs** — `Password::parse()` with length validation, `Password::hash()` consuming self, `PasswordHash_` separate type.
   - **src/domain/todo_item.rs** — `TodoItem` enum with Pending/Completed variants, `complete()` and `uncomplete()` state transitions.
   - **src/domain/todo_title.rs** — `TodoTitle` parse-don't-validate, max 300 chars, trim, non-empty.
   - **src/infrastructure/user_repository.rs** — `insert_user()`, `find_user_by_email()`.
   - **src/infrastructure/todo_repository.rs** — `insert_todo()`, `find_todos_by_user()`, `find_todo_by_id()`, `update_todo_completion()`, `update_todo_title()`, `delete_todo()`.
   - **src/services/registration.rs** — `register_user()` with tracing instrumentation.
   - **src/services/authentication.rs** — `authenticate_user()` with generic `InvalidCredentials` error.
   - **src/services/todo_service.rs** — `add_todo()`, `get_todos()`, `toggle_todo_completion()`, `update_todo_title()`, `delete_todo()` with auth checks.
   - **src/startup.rs** — Application builder with Router, DB pool, middleware, session store (`PostgresStore::migrate()`), auto-migrations.
   - **static/css/main.css** — Design tokens, cascade layers, auth-form component, todo-item component, skip-link, focus-visible, custom checkbox, delete confirmation CSS.
   - **tests/api/** — Integration test suite with `TestApp`/`spawn_app()` pattern, unique DB per test.
   - **docs/glossary.md** — Domain language mapping updated throughout.
   - **.sqlx/** — Offline query cache for CI.

4. Errors and Fixes:
   - **Team never pushing commits**: The dominant issue. Teammates would commit locally but not push, or write code without committing at all. Required 4+ explicit requests per push cycle. Fixed by adopting commit discipline rules and persistent reminders.
   - **tower-sessions version incompatibility**: `tower-sessions 0.13` uses `axum-core 0.4`, incompatible with Axum 0.8's `axum-core 0.5`. Fixed by bumping to `tower-sessions 0.14` + `tower-sessions-sqlx-store 0.15` (commit `e2cda97`).
   - **`Redirect::see_other()` doesn't exist in Axum 0.8**: Fixed by using `Redirect::to()` which returns 303 See Other.
   - **Axum 0.8 path parameter syntax**: `/todos/:id/toggle` should be `/todos/{id}/toggle`. Fixed by Scott.
   - **Tests committed without implementation (RED state)**: Commit `79db2c3` committed POST /register tests without the handler. Subsequent commits (`cd589b2`, `4591bc0`) fixed by adding the handler.
   - **CI PostgreSQL not configured**: Integration tests failed in CI because no PostgreSQL service was available. Fixed by adding `services: postgres:` section to ci.yml (commit `ac15c21`).
   - **SQLx offline cache missing test queries**: `cargo sqlx prepare` needs `-- --tests` flag. Fixed by using `DATABASE_URL` directly in CI.
   - **Askama HTML entity encoding**: Tests checked for `&#x27;` but Askama outputs `&#39;`. Fixed by making assertions encoding-agnostic.
   - **Session store schema mismatch**: `tower-sessions-sqlx-store 0.15` expects schema-qualified table. Fixed by calling `PostgresStore::migrate()` in startup.
   - **Registration a11y issues (4 items)**: Error elements conditionally rendered, missing password hint, `minlength` attribute, wrong redirect. Fixed in commit `6c757bc`.
   - **Task 5 marked complete prematurely** (multiple times): Reverted to in_progress each time until a11y issues were actually fixed and CI green.
   - **Teammates skipping ahead to future tasks**: Team built Task 7 code while Task 5 a11y issues were unresolved. Required broadcasts to stop work.

5. Problem Solving:
   - **Commit discipline**: The core process problem. Solved by proposing, getting consensus (9/9), and adding 5 rules to TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md. The rules directly address every recurring issue: not committing (Rule 1), not verifying CI (Rule 2), marking tasks done prematurely (Rule 3), leftover files between tasks (Rule 4), leaving broken code (Rule 5).
   - **Task ordering enforcement**: Team repeatedly jumped ahead (starting Task 6 before Task 5 a11y fixes, starting Task 7 before Task 5 complete). Solved by broadcasting stop orders and reverting task statuses.
   - **MVP completion**: All 10 feature tasks completed with 48 integration tests. The no-JS baseline is functional for all user stories.
   - **Outstanding a11y issues** (noted but not blocking MVP): Toggle checkbox semantics, conditional error divs in 3 templates, edit page error pattern.
   - **Post-MVP tasks created**: Tasks #21-24 (delete confirmation, HTMX enhancement, aria-live, password toggle) created by Marty but not started.

6. All User Messages:
   - "what rules could the team put in place to clean up their behavior?"

<teammate-message teammate_id="marty-cagan" color="blue" summary="Product assessment and task prioritization for MVP polish">
I've reviewed PROJECT.md, TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md, the user stories, and the full task list. Here's my product assessment:

**Current State**: The core MVP features (US-1 through US-8) are all built and working with 48 integration tests passing. What remains are polish tasks to bring the app up to our Definition of Done -- specifically a11y fixes, HTMX enhancement, aria-live regions, and the password toggle.

**Task Priorities (product perspective)**:

1. **Task #1** (a11y error elements) -- In progress with Luca. This is critical: screen readers can't properly announce form errors without it. Must finish first.

2. **Task #2** (Forgot password link) -- Quick win. US-2 explicitly requires this link. It's a simple placeholder page but users expect to see it on a login form. Should be picked up by whoever is free after Task #1.

3. **Task #3** (HTMX enhancement) -- This is the biggest remaining piece and it unlocks Task #4. Without HTMX, every operation causes a full page reload, which works but isn't the experience we want. This is what makes it feel like a modern app while still working without JS.

4. **Task #4** (aria-live announcements) -- Blocked by #3. Once HTMX is in, we need screen reader announcements for dynamic updates. Required by our Definition of Done.

5. **Task #5** (Password visibility toggle) -- Independent of #3/#4. TypeScript progressive enhancement per the team's consensus in US-1. Can be done in parallel with HTMX work.

**My recommendation**: Once Task #1 is done and committed, the team should split into two parallel streams:
- Stream A: Tasks #3 then #4 (HTMX + aria-live) -- this is the critical path
- Stream B: Tasks #2 and #5 (forgot password + password toggle) -- independent work

However, per our commit discipline and mob programming rules, only one person drives at a time. So the sequencing is: finish #1, then work through #2-#5 in priority order, with #3 taking precedence since it unblocks #4.

I'm ready to provide product context, validate features against acceptance criteria, and review copy/UX as the team works through these tasks. Let me know what the team needs from me.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="steve-krug" color="red" summary="UX review of all templates and pending tasks">
I've read PROJECT.md, TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md, and reviewed all the templates and CSS. Here's my UX assessment of the current state and the pending tasks.

**Current State UX Review:**

The app is in solid shape for an MVP. The templates are clean, the copy is concise, and the flows are straightforward. Some specific observations:

1. **Login page (login.html):** Good -- "Sign in" heading, clear labels, "Don't have an account? Create account" link at the bottom. The form remembers the email on error (good). Missing: "Forgot password?" link per Task #2.

2. **Registration page (register.html):** Good -- clear labels, password hint ("At least 8 characters"), confirmation field, and the "Already have an account? Sign in" cross-link. Error handling with aria-describedby is the reference pattern for Task #1.

3. **Todo list page (todos.html):** 
   - The add form is clear: label "New todo", placeholder "What do you need to do?", "Add todo" button. 
   - The empty state ("No todos yet.") is minimal and appropriate.
   - The delete confirmation using details/summary is clever -- no JS required for the two-step confirm.
   - One concern: the toggle icons (checkbox characters) and edit/delete icons are Unicode characters. They work, but the aria-labels are what really matters here, and those are well done.

4. **Edit page (edit_todo.html):** Clean. "Save" and "Cancel" buttons are clear. The autofocus on the title input is correct UX.

5. **Index page (index.html):** "Welcome" + "A simple todo list application." -- This page is essentially a landing page. For authenticated users who navigate here, they'd probably expect to be redirected to /todos. For unauthenticated users, they'd want sign in/register links. Currently bare.

**On the pending tasks:**

- **Task #2 (Forgot password? link):** I fully support this. It's a standard convention users expect on any login form. The placeholder page should be friendly: something like "Password reset is coming soon. For now, please contact support if you're locked out." Keep it short. No happy talk.

- **Task #3 (HTMX enhancement):** From a UX perspective, this is the highest-impact improvement. Full page reloads after adding/toggling/deleting a todo item disrupt the user's flow. HTMX will make the experience feel natural -- add a todo, it appears in the list, no page jump. Critical for usability.

- **Task #5 (Password visibility toggle):** Nice progressive enhancement. The pattern of replacing the confirm field when the toggle is active is smart -- if you can see what you're typing, you don't need to confirm it.

I'm ready to review any in-progress work and provide usability feedback. I can also help with copy and label decisions for any of these tasks. Let me know where you need me.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="lea-verou" color="pink" summary="Task #5 plan ready, awaiting driver rotation">
While waiting for the driver rotation, I've prepared my plan for Task #5 (password visibility toggle). Here's what I'm thinking:

**Architecture decisions needed (for mob discussion):**

1. **TypeScript tooling**: No TS infrastructure exists yet. We need:
   - `typescript` added to flake.nix buildInputs (or `esbuild` which is faster and simpler)
   - A `tsconfig.json` for type checking
   - Source in something like `ts/` and compiled output in `static/js/`
   - A simple build command (no bundler needed for vanilla TS)

2. **Script loading**: The base template has `{% block scripts %}` ready. The register template would include `<script src="/static/js/password-toggle.js" defer></script>` in that block.

3. **Progressive enhancement approach** (per US-1):
   - No-JS baseline: email + password + password confirmation (already works)
   - JS enhancement: Add toggle button after password input, toggle input type between password/text, update aria-label/aria-pressed, remove/restore confirm field when toggle is active
   - The confirm field serves as the no-JS substitute for "let me see what I typed"

4. **A11y requirements**:
   - Toggle button must be `type="button"` (not submit)
   - `aria-label` switches between "Show password" / "Hide password"
   - `aria-pressed` reflects state
   - Focus stays on toggle after activation
   - The confirm field removal should not cause focus loss

I'm ready to drive whenever task #1 is committed and pushed. Please let me know when it's my turn.
</teammate-message>

**Task #2 (Forgot password?) placement note:** The link should go between the "Sign in" button and the "Don't have an account?" footer text. <teammate-message teammate_id="carson-gross" color="yellow" summary="Carson standing by, design notes ready for #3">

This keeps the progressive enhancement clean.

<teammate-message teammate_id="steve-schoger" color="cyan" summary="Design review notes: CSS gaps and Task #2 spec">
Standing by per instructions -- not touching files. Here are my design observations for when Luca finishes Task #1 and the team reviews:

**CSS gaps to address (either in Task #1 or as follow-up):**

1. **`todo-add__error` has no CSS rule.** The class is used in `todos.html` (line 32) but there's no matching style in `main.css`. It needs at minimum:
   - `color: var(--color-danger)` and `font-size: var(--font-size-sm)` to match the `auth-form__error` pattern
   - An empty state should collapse visually (`:empty { display: none }` or similar) so it doesn't create dead space when there's no error

2. **`nav-logout` / `nav-logout__button` have no CSS rules.** Both `todos.html` and `edit_todo.html` use these classes in their nav blocks, but the CSS has `.site-header` / `.site-header__brand` / `.site-header__actions` instead. Either the templates should use the existing site-header classes, or we need nav-logout CSS.

**For Task #2 (forgot password link) -- design spec:**
- Place the link between the submit button and the footer text
- Style: same as `auth-form__footer` -- small, muted, centered
- Text: "Forgot your password?" as a link
- The placeholder page should use `auth-form` layout with a friendly heading and one sentence explaining the feature is coming

These are review notes only -- I'm not making any changes.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="lea-verou" color="pink" summary="Task #5 prep complete, flagged design question">
Preparation for task #5 is complete. I've reviewed register.rs, register.html, the test suite, flake.nix, and the static file structure.

One design question I want to flag for the mob when we get to task #5: When the JS toggle removes the confirm field from the DOM, the form won't submit a `password_confirmation` value. The server expects it in `RegisterFormData`. My preferred approach is to insert a hidden input that mirrors the password value when the toggle is active, so the server contract is maintained without backend changes. This keeps it purely a frontend progressive enhancement with zero Rust changes.

<teammate-message teammate_id="steve-schoger" color="cyan" summary="Design review done, flagging 4 CSS gaps">
Design review of Tasks #1 and #2 -- both look good. The a11y error patterns are correct and the forgot password page is clean.

I want to flag a few minor CSS gaps that still exist. These won't block Task #3 but should be addressed at some point:

1. **`todo-add__error`** -- used in todos.html but still has no CSS rule. Error text will render in default body color/size instead of danger red/small like `auth-form__error`.
2. **`nav-logout` / `nav-logout__button`** -- templates use these classes but CSS only has `.site-header` classes. The logout button is probably getting base button styles (blue, padded) when it should be styled as a text-link action.
3. **`.auth-form__message` when empty** -- the login page always renders the error div, but when empty it still gets `padding` and `margin-block-end` from `.auth-form__message`, creating a visible gap. Should collapse with `:empty { display: none }`.
4. **`.auth-form__cancel`** -- used on edit_todo.html but no CSS rule exists.

None of these block Carson. Standing by in review mode for Task #3.
</teammate-message>

3. Add todo: hx-post, hx-target=".todo-list", hx-swap="beforeend", form resets on success

6. All three handlers detect HX-Request header for fragment vs redirect responses
7. App still works without JavaScript (progressive enhancement)

<teammate-message teammate_id="steve-krug" color="red" summary="UX review of Tasks 3 and 5 - no issues">
Pulled latest (649fb5d) and reviewed Tasks #3 and #5. UX assessment:

**Task #3 (HTMX enhancement) -- solid work by Carson.**
- The todo_item.html partial is clean -- each item is self-contained with its own hx-post/hx-target/hx-swap attributes. Locality of behavior is respected.
- Add form: `hx-on::after-request="if(event.detail.successful) this.reset()"` -- good, clears the input after successful add. The rapid entry pattern works.
- Toggle: `hx-target="#todo-{{ todo.id }}" hx-swap="outerHTML"` -- replaces just the item, no page reload. Clean.
- Delete: same outerHTML swap pattern on the individual item. When the server returns empty, the item disappears.
- The list is always in the DOM now (with `hidden` attribute when empty), which is necessary for hx-target to have a swap target. Smart structural change.
- Edit link still navigates to `/todos/{id}/edit` (no inline editing via HTMX yet). That's fine for this iteration -- it works.
- Progressive enhancement preserved: forms still have `method="post"` and `action` attributes, so no-JS still works.

**Task #5 (Password visibility toggle) -- well done by Lea.**
- The IIFE pattern is clean and self-contained.
- Graceful degradation: only runs if both `#password` and `#confirm-group` exist. If JS fails, the baseline form with both password fields still works.
- The toggle removes the confirm field from the DOM entirely (not just hidden), which is correct -- hidden fields still submit form data and could confuse server-side validation.
- `aria-pressed` and `aria-label` update correctly on toggle. Screen readers will announce the state change.
- The confirm field is restored to its original DOM position when toggling back, preserving tab order.
- One UX note: the toggle text "Show password" / "Hide password" is clear and conventional. No issues.

**No blocking UX concerns on any completed task.** Everything follows the patterns we agreed on. Ready for final review after Task #4 lands.

<teammate-message teammate_id="carson-gross" color="yellow" summary="Focus management follow-ups from Steve's UX review">
Steve Krug sent good focus management guidance. Task #3 already handles some of it (add input clears on success, toggle keeps focus, no-JS works). But there are follow-up items that go beyond Task #3 and #4:

1. **Delete focus management**: After deleting, focus should move to the next todo item (or previous, or the add input if list is now empty). This needs a JS event listener on htmx:afterSwap.

2. **Empty state on last delete**: When the last item is deleted via HTMX, the "No todos yet." text doesn't reappear. The hidden `<ul>` gets emptied but the empty state paragraph isn't shown. Could use HX-Trigger + out-of-band swap or a small JS listener.

3. **Inline edit mode**: Task #3 doesn't include inline editing via HTMX (the edit link still navigates to the separate edit page). Inline editing with focus management would be a separate enhancement.

These could be tracked as new tasks if the team wants to address them. They're polish-on-polish -- the core HTMX functionality works correctly.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="lea-verou" color="pink" summary="Reviewed tasks #3 and #5, flagged password toggle issue">
Pulled latest (649fb5d) and reviewed tasks #3 and #5. Here's my assessment:

**Task #3 (HTMX) -- looks good:**
- Locality of behavior principle followed: each HTMX-enhanced element is self-describing
- Todo item extracted to `todo_item.html` partial -- clean for fragment responses
- The `ul.todo-list` now always renders (with `hidden` attribute when empty) so `hx-swap="beforeend"` has a target
- Form reset via `hx-on::after-request` is a nice touch
- No CSS concerns

**Task #5 (Password toggle) -- looks good with one concern:**
- Progressive enhancement is correct: IIFE with graceful bailout
- `aria-pressed` and `aria-label` properly toggled
- CSS is minimal and appropriate (text-link style using tokens)
- Confirm group DOM position preserved for restore

**One concern to flag for later:** When the toggle is active (password visible, confirm field removed from DOM), the form submits without a `password_confirmation` field. Axum's `Form` deserializer will likely reject this with a 422 error since `password_confirmation` is a required `String` field in `RegisterFormData`. The user would see a generic error rather than a helpful message. 

This could be fixed by either:
- (A) Adding a hidden input that mirrors the password value when toggle is active (my original suggestion)
- (B) Making `password_confirmation` optional in the form data and skipping the mismatch check when it's absent

This is not a blocker for the current sprint -- the no-JS baseline works correctly and users can toggle back to restore the field. But it should be tracked as a follow-up.

Standing by while Luca finishes task #4.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="heydon-pickering" color="green" summary="All tasks complete, Task #4 a11y review approved">
All 5 tasks are now completed. Here is my a11y review of Kent Beck's Task #4 (aria-live announcements, commit 554c928):

**Verdict: Approved -- implementation is correct and accessible.**

Key findings:

1. **HX-Trigger event detail structure is correct.** I verified via the HTMX documentation (Context7) that when the server sends `HX-Trigger: {"announce":"Todo added"}`, the client receives a custom event where `evt.detail.value === "Todo added"`. The listener in `base.html` correctly accesses `e.detail.value`.

2. **Live region setup is sound.** The `#live-region` div has `aria-live="polite"` and `aria-atomic="true"`, which means screen readers will announce the full content of the region when it changes, without interrupting the user mid-task. The `polite` assertiveness level is the right choice for these non-urgent status messages.

3. **Announce messages are clear and concise:**
   - "Todo added" -- for successful add
   - "Todo completed" / "Todo marked pending" -- for toggle (context-aware)
   - "Todo deleted" -- for delete
   These are appropriately brief and informative for screen reader users.

4. **Tests are comprehensive.** Three new tests verify that each HTMX operation (add, toggle, delete) returns the `HX-Trigger` header containing the `announce` event with the expected message content.

5. **The `visually-hidden` class** on the live region correctly hides it visually while keeping it available to assistive technology.

**Overall a11y status of the project (comprehensive audit):**
- All forms have always-in-DOM error elements with `role="alert"` and `aria-describedby`
- Error states correctly set `aria-invalid="true"` 
- Skip link, landmarks (header/nav/main/footer), and semantic structure are solid
- Toggle/delete/edit buttons all have accessible labels including the todo title
- Password toggle has `aria-pressed` and `aria-label` state management
- Dynamic HTMX updates now have live region announcements

**Future considerations** (not blockers for MVP):
- Focus management after HTMX swaps (e.g., after adding a todo, focus could move to the new item)
- The `details/summary` delete confirmation pattern has inconsistent screen reader support across platforms -- may want to test with VoiceOver/NVDA
- Consider `aria-live="assertive"` for error announcements if users report missing them

All tasks complete. I am idle and available for new work.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="heydon-pickering" color="green" summary="Task #1 a11y review: approved, all patterns correct">
Here is my a11y review of Task #1 (commit 9cdc020) -- always-in-DOM error elements.

**Verdict: Approved with one minor note.**

Checking against the five criteria:

**1. All error elements always in the DOM (empty when no error) -- PASS**
- `login.html:8` -- Error div is always rendered; uses `{% if let Some(error) = error_message %}{{ error }}{% endif %}` so it's present but empty when no error.
- `todos.html:33` -- `<p id="add-todo-error" ...>` always in DOM, conditionally populated.
- `edit_todo.html:14` -- General error div always present (same pattern as login).
- `edit_todo.html:29` -- `<p id="title-error" ...>` always in DOM, conditionally populated.

**2. role="alert" on error elements -- PASS**
- `login.html:8` -- `role="alert"` present on error div.
- `todos.html:33` -- `role="alert"` present on error paragraph.
- `edit_todo.html:14` -- `role="alert"` on general error div.
- `edit_todo.html:29` -- `role="alert"` on title-error paragraph.

**3. aria-describedby always references error element IDs -- PASS**
- `todos.html:26` -- `aria-describedby="add-todo-error"` always set on title input.
- `edit_todo.html:26` -- `aria-describedby="title-error"` always set on title input.
- `login.html` -- Note: the login form does NOT use `aria-describedby` on individual inputs; the error is a general message at the top (like "Invalid email or password"). This is acceptable because login errors are intentionally vague for security (no per-field validation), and the `role="alert"` on the error div ensures screen readers announce it.

**4. aria-invalid only set when there IS an error -- PASS**
- `todos.html:27` -- `{% if error_message.is_some() %}aria-invalid="true"{% endif %}` -- conditional.
- `edit_todo.html:27` -- `{% if error_message.is_some() %}aria-invalid="true"{% endif %}` -- conditional.
- `login.html` -- No `aria-invalid` used at all, which is correct since login doesn't do per-field validation.

**5. Pattern matches register.html (the reference) -- PASS**
The register.html reference pattern is:
- Error `<p>` always in DOM with `id`, `role="alert"`, conditionally populated
- Input has `aria-describedby` always set to the error element ID
- `aria-invalid="true"` conditionally set only when error exists

All three modified templates follow this pattern.

**Minor note (not a blocker):** The login error div on line 8 does not have an `id` attribute. If we ever want to add `aria-describedby` to the login inputs (e.g., for a per-field validation future), we would need to add one. For now this is fine since the general error approach with `role="alert"` works correctly for the login use case.

All good. Task #1 is solid from an accessibility perspective.
</teammate-message>

## 2026-02-08 21:58 UTC -- User

<teammate-message teammate_id="luca-palmieri" color="yellow" summary="Retrospective proposals from Luca Palmieri">
Here are my retrospective proposals. I am approaching this as an engineering problem: our current architecture has a fundamental concurrency bug, and social rules alone cannot fix it.

## Diagnosis

The root cause of our problems is **shared mutable state without synchronization**. Nine agents share one filesystem and one git working tree. The "one driver" rule is a social mutex, and social mutexes fail under load -- exactly as we observed. This is the same problem as multiple threads writing to shared memory without a lock. No amount of documentation fixes a race condition.

## Proposal 1: Reduce Active Writers to ONE (Strongest Recommendation)

**Problem**: 9 agents with write access = 9 potential concurrent writers. Social coordination failed repeatedly.

**Solution**: Only ONE agent should have write access at any time. The rest are reviewers/advisors who participate through messaging only.

**Concrete change to CLAUDE.md**:
- The coordinator spawns exactly ONE "driver" agent at a time with write access
- All other team members participate as **advisory voices through the messaging system** -- they review, suggest, critique, but do not touch files
- When the driver needs a different specialty (e.g., switching from Rust backend work to CSS), the coordinator shuts down the current driver and spawns a new one with the appropriate profile
- Multiple advisors CAN be spawned simultaneously since they only read and message

This is not "reducing the team" -- it is enforcing the mob programming model we already agreed to. In real mob programming, there is literally one keyboard. We need to enforce that constraint architecturally, not socially.

## Proposal 2: Single Composite Driver Agent

**Problem**: Even with one driver, swapping agents is slow and loses context.

**Solution**: Instead of spawning separate agents for each persona, spawn ONE driver agent whose prompt includes the relevant expertise from multiple profiles. For example, when building a feature that touches Rust + HTMX + CSS, the driver prompt includes guidance from Luca, Carson, and Lea's profiles. The coordinator assembles the right "composite persona" for each task.

**Benefits**:
- Zero concurrent writers (there is literally one agent)
- No context-switching overhead between drivers
- The mob's collective knowledge is embedded in the driver's prompt
- No coordination protocol needed -- one agent, one filesystem, one git history

**Trade-off**: A single agent has a finite context window and cannot hold all 9 profiles simultaneously. The coordinator would need to select the 2-4 most relevant profiles per task.

## Proposal 3: Strict Git-Based Handoff Protocol (If Multiple Agents Are Retained)

If the team decides to keep multiple active agents, we need a mechanical (not social) handoff:

**Add to TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md under Commit Discipline**:

```
### Driver Handoff Protocol

1. Before any file modification, the driver runs `git status` and confirms the working tree is clean.
2. After completing a unit of work (green tests), the driver commits, pushes, and confirms CI green.
3. The driver sends a "HANDOFF" message to the coordinator with the commit SHA.
4. The coordinator confirms the handoff and designates the next driver.
5. The next driver runs `git pull` before touching any file.
6. NO agent may modify files without being explicitly designated as the current driver by the coordinator.

Violation of this protocol (editing files when not the designated driver) is treated as a production incident.
```

## Proposal 4: Task Granularity and Gating

**Problem**: Agents started future tasks early, marked tasks complete before CI verified, and accumulated uncommitted work.

**Add to TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md**:

```
### Task Completion Gating

A task may ONLY be marked "completed" when ALL of the following are true:
1. All code changes are committed and pushed
2. CI has passed (verified via `gh run list --limit 1`)
3. The coordinator has acknowledged the completion

No agent may begin work on a new task until:
1. Their current task is marked completed (with the above gates)
2. The coordinator has assigned them the next task

Tasks should be small enough to complete in a single driver session (one TDD cycle: red-green-refactor for one behavior).
```

## Proposal 5: Remove CLAUDE.md Instruction for Teammates to NOT Read It

**Problem**: CLAUDE.md says "Teammates should NOT read this file." But teammates need to understand the coordination model to follow it.

**Solution**: Split CLAUDE.md into two files:
- `CLAUDE.md` -- coordinator-only instructions (spawning, delegation)
- `COORDINATION.md` -- the driver/advisor protocol, handoff rules, task gating. All agents read this.

This way the coordination rules are visible to everyone, while the coordinator-specific launch instructions remain separate.

## My Ranking

1. **Proposal 1 + 2 (composite driver)** -- This is the correct architectural solution. One writer, period. It mirrors real mob programming. Everything else is a workaround.
2. **Proposal 3 (git handoff protocol)** -- If we must have multiple agents, this is the minimum viable coordination.
3. **Proposal 4 (task gating)** -- Necessary regardless of which model we adopt.
4. **Proposal 5 (split CLAUDE.md)** -- Low effort, improves transparency.

From a production engineering perspective: you do not solve concurrency bugs by writing better comments. You solve them by eliminating the shared mutable state or by introducing proper synchronization primitives. Proposal 1+2 eliminates the problem. Proposal 3 introduces synchronization. I strongly favor elimination over synchronization.

</teammate-message>

## 2026-02-08 21:59 UTC -- User

<teammate-message teammate_id="kent-beck" color="blue" summary="Driver-Reviewer model proposal for all three docs">
Here are my retrospective proposals. I've thought hard about this, drawing on decades of watching teams struggle with coordination overhead vs. actual programming.

## Diagnosis

The root cause is **structural, not behavioral**. We wrote rules ("one driver at a time") that require voluntary compliance in an environment where compliance is mechanically impossible to enforce. Nine agents share one filesystem and one branch. When Agent A writes a file, Agent B's read of that file changes underneath them. No amount of "please don't touch the keyboard" agreements can fix a shared mutable state problem. We need immutable architecture, not better manners.

This is exactly the pattern I've seen in real teams: when a practice keeps failing despite everyone agreeing to follow it, the practice doesn't fit the environment. Change the environment, not the people.

## Proposal: The Driver-Reviewer Model

### Core Structural Change

**Reduce from 9 concurrent write-capable agents to 1.** At any given time, exactly ONE agent has write access. The others participate through review and messaging only.

This isn't reducing team size -- it's making the mob pattern actually work for AI agents. In a real mob, only one person has the keyboard. We just need to enforce that mechanically.

### How It Works

1. **The Coordinator spawns ONE "Driver" agent** with full tool access (Read, Write, Edit, Bash).
2. **The Coordinator spawns Reviewer agents** as needed -- these agents can Read files and send messages, but do NOT write code. They review, advise, catch issues, and propose changes via messages to the Driver.
3. **The Driver does all file modifications, commits, and pushes.**
4. **When the Driver completes a task** (committed, pushed, CI green), the Coordinator can:
   - Keep the same Driver for the next task, or
   - Shut down the current Driver and spawn a new one with a different persona

### Why This Works

- **Mechanically prevents concurrent edits**: Only one agent can write.
- **Preserves mob wisdom**: Reviewers provide all the multi-perspective value (a11y, design, domain, UX) without filesystem conflicts.
- **Simplifies commit discipline**: One agent writes, commits, pushes. No coordination needed.
- **Reduces cost**: We don't need 9 full agents running simultaneously. Spawn reviewers on demand.

### Practical Reviewer Usage

Not all 9 personas need to be active simultaneously. For a backend database task, you'd spawn:
- **Driver**: Luca (Rust engineer)
- **Reviewers**: Kent (TDD), Scott (domain types), maybe Heydon (if there's HTML output)

For a CSS/design task:
- **Driver**: Lea (CSS)
- **Reviewers**: Steve Schoger (design), Heydon (a11y), Carson (HTMX integration)

The Coordinator picks the right subset for each task.

---

## Specific Document Changes

### CLAUDE.md (Coordinator Instructions)

Replace the current "Launching Teammates" and "Teammate Permissions" sections with:

```markdown
## Launching Teammates

### Driver Agent (exactly one at a time)
- Launch ONE driver agent with full tool access (`subagent_type: "general-purpose"`)
- Include the teammate's `.team/` profile content in the prompt
- Instruct the driver to read `PROJECT.md` and `TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md`
- The driver is responsible for ALL file modifications, git operations, and CI verification
- Only ONE driver agent may exist at any time. Shut down the current driver before spawning a new one.

### Reviewer Agents (zero or more)
- Launch reviewer agents as needed for the current task
- Reviewers are spawned with `subagent_type: "general-purpose"` but their prompt MUST include this instruction:
  "You are in REVIEWER mode. You may READ files and SEND MESSAGES but you must NOT use Write, Edit, or Bash tools that modify files or run git commands. Your role is to review the Driver's work, suggest improvements, catch issues, and provide expertise via messages."
- Reviewers provide domain expertise, catch bugs, review a11y, suggest design improvements -- all via messages to the Driver
- Spawn only the reviewers relevant to the current task (typically 2-4, not all 8)

### Task Workflow
1. Coordinator creates a task and assigns a Driver persona
2. Coordinator spawns the Driver agent
3. Coordinator spawns relevant Reviewer agents
4. Driver works through Red-Green-Refactor, committing and pushing at each green step
5. Driver messages Coordinator when task is complete (committed, pushed, CI green)
6. Coordinator verifies CI, then shuts down agents before starting the next task
```

### TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md Changes

Replace the "Mob/Ensemble Programming" section with:

```markdown
### Driver-Reviewer Model
- **One Driver, multiple Reviewers.** Exactly one agent modifies files at any time.
  The Driver writes code, runs tests, commits, and pushes. Reviewers provide expertise
  via messages only.
- **The Driver owns the keyboard.** No reviewer may modify files. All suggestions flow
  through messages. The Driver decides how to incorporate feedback.
- **Reviewers are the mob's eyes.** They read code, check accessibility, verify design
  tokens, validate domain modeling, and catch issues the Driver might miss. Their value
  is in perspective, not keystrokes.
- **Rotate by task, not by timer.** When a task is complete, the Coordinator may assign
  a different persona as Driver for the next task based on the expertise needed.
- **The Driver follows TDD discipline.** Red-Green-Refactor with commits at every green
  step. The Reviewers hold the Driver accountable via messages: "I notice we haven't
  written a test for that error case yet."
```

Replace the "Commit Discipline" section with:

```markdown
### Commit Discipline

1. **Commit at every green step.** When `cargo fmt --check`, `cargo clippy -- -D warnings`,
   and `cargo test` all pass, commit immediately.
2. **Push immediately after every commit.** Run `git push` right after `git commit`.
   Verify CI with `gh run list --limit 1` and wait for green before writing new code.
3. **Only the Driver commits.** Since only one agent has write access, there is no risk
   of concurrent commits. The Driver is solely responsible for the commit-push-verify cycle.
4. **If CI fails, the Driver fixes it before any new work.** Red CI is the top priority.
5. **Task is not complete until CI is green.** The Driver must verify CI passes before
   reporting task completion to the Coordinator.
```

### PROJECT.md Changes

Add to the "Development Mandates" section:

```markdown
- **Driver-Reviewer Model**: At most one agent may modify files at any time (the Driver).
  Other agents participate as Reviewers via read-only access and messaging. This replaces
  the traditional mob "one keyboard" rule with a mechanically enforced equivalent.
```

---

## What We Lose and Why It's Worth It

**We lose**: The feeling that "everyone is coding together." Some reviewers may feel less engaged.

**We gain**: 
- Zero concurrent edit conflicts (mechanically impossible)
- Clean commit history (one author per task)
- Reliable CI verification (one agent responsible)
- Lower cost (fewer concurrent agents)
- The actual benefits of mob programming (multiple perspectives) without the coordination nightmare

**The key insight**: The value of mob programming was never that multiple people type simultaneously. It was that multiple perspectives apply to the same code at the same time. The Driver-Reviewer model preserves that value while eliminating the shared-mutable-state problem.

This is the XP principle of "turning the knobs to 10" applied to our situation. If only one person should drive, make it so only one person *can* drive.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="scott-wlaschin" color="green" summary="Retrospective proposals for process improvements">
Here are my retrospective proposals from a type-driven / "make illegal states unrepresentable" perspective.

## Root Cause Analysis

The fundamental problem is that we tried to enforce a **sequential constraint** (one driver at a time) using a **social rule** in a **concurrent system** (9 autonomous agents sharing one filesystem). This is exactly analogous to using runtime validation instead of compile-time types -- it fails under pressure because nothing structurally prevents the invalid state.

In domain modeling terms: our process allowed an "illegal state" -- multiple agents writing concurrently -- to be representable. We relied on agents voluntarily checking whether they were the driver, which is like relying on callers to remember to call `validate()` before using a value. It never works reliably.

## Proposal 1: Reduce the Team to 3 Active Agents (STRONGLY RECOMMENDED)

**The problem**: 9 agents sharing one working directory cannot enforce sequential access. The "mob" model assumes humans sitting around one screen -- a physical constraint that enforces single-driver. Agents have no such physical constraint.

**The solution**: Restructure the team into 3 roles that map to the actual execution model:

| Role | Agent | Responsibility |
|------|-------|---------------|
| **Driver** | 1 agent (Luca, the lead Rust engineer) | Writes ALL code. The only agent with write access to the codebase. |
| **Navigator** | 1 agent (rotating persona) | Reviews Driver's work, suggests direction, catches issues. Does NOT write code. Communicates via messages only. |
| **Reviewer** | 1 agent (rotating persona) | Reviews commits after push, checks a11y/UX/design/domain concerns. Does NOT write code. |

The key insight: **the Driver is a singleton**. Just like a database write lock. Only one agent ever touches files. The Navigator and Reviewer influence the code through messages to the Driver, never by editing files directly.

The 9 team member *personas* still exist -- they rotate through the Navigator and Reviewer slots. When we need domain architecture input, the Navigator embodies Scott Wlaschin. When we need a11y review, the Reviewer embodies Heydon Pickering. But structurally, only 3 agents are alive at once, and only 1 writes code.

**Changes to CLAUDE.md**: The coordinator spawns exactly 3 agents. The Driver agent's prompt includes ALL team personas relevant to the current task (it internalizes the full mob's knowledge). Navigator and Reviewer agents embody specific personas based on what the current task needs.

**Changes to TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md**: Replace the "Mob/Ensemble Programming" section entirely:

```markdown
### Driver-Navigator-Reviewer Model

All code changes follow a strict Driver-Navigator-Reviewer model:

- **Driver (1 agent)**: The ONLY agent that reads, writes, edits files, runs commands, 
  and makes commits. Currently: Luca Palmieri. The Driver internalizes guidance from 
  all team personas but is the sole executor.
- **Navigator (1 agent)**: Provides direction, catches design issues, suggests approaches. 
  Communicates ONLY via messages to the Driver. Never touches files. Persona rotates 
  based on task needs (e.g., Scott for domain modeling, Carson for HTMX patterns).
- **Reviewer (1 agent)**: Reviews completed commits for quality, a11y, UX, design 
  consistency. Communicates ONLY via messages. Persona rotates based on task needs 
  (e.g., Heydon for a11y, Steve Krug for usability).

This model makes concurrent file editing structurally impossible -- only one agent 
has file access.
```

## Proposal 2: Enforce Commit-Push-Verify as an Atomic Operation

**The problem**: Even with one Driver, we had commits without pushes and work started before CI verified.

**The solution**: Define a `GreenStep` as an atomic workflow that the Driver must complete before any new work:

```
Write Code -> cargo fmt -> cargo clippy -> cargo test -> git commit -> git push -> gh run list (verify green)
```

This is a pipeline -- each step's success is the precondition for the next. You cannot skip ahead. In type-system terms, the "state" of work progresses through:

```
Editing -> LocallyVerified -> Committed -> Pushed -> CIGreen
```

And only at `CIGreen` can you transition back to `Editing` for the next change.

**Changes to TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md** (Commit Discipline section):

```markdown
### Commit Discipline (Atomic Green Step)

Every code change follows the Green Step pipeline. Each step MUST complete 
successfully before proceeding to the next:

1. Write/edit code (smallest meaningful change)
2. `cargo fmt --check` (fix if needed)
3. `cargo clippy -- -D warnings` (fix if needed)  
4. `cargo test` (fix if needed)
5. `git add` + `git commit` (with descriptive message)
6. `git push`
7. `gh run list --limit 1` -- wait for CI to complete green
8. ONLY THEN begin the next change

If ANY step fails, fix it before proceeding. No new work until CI is green.
The Driver must report the CI status to the Navigator before starting new work.
```

## Proposal 3: Task Completion Requires CI Proof

**The problem**: Tasks were marked complete before CI verified the code.

**The solution**: Add to Definition of Done:

```markdown
### Process
- [ ] CI pipeline has passed on the pushed commit (verified via `gh run list`)
- [ ] The commit SHA that CI verified matches the commit that implements the feature
```

A task is NOT complete until the CI run ID and green status are confirmed. The Reviewer agent's job includes verifying this before agreeing that a task is done.

## Proposal 4: Simplify the Coordinator's Job

**Changes to CLAUDE.md**: Since we're going from 9 agents to 3, the coordinator becomes simpler:

- Spawn Driver, Navigator, Reviewer at session start
- Assign personas to Navigator and Reviewer based on current task
- Relay escalations to project owner
- Verify task completion includes CI proof

## Summary

The core philosophy: **make the illegal state (concurrent editing) structurally impossible** rather than relying on social rules. The Driver-Navigator-Reviewer model with a single file-touching agent is the structural enforcement. The atomic Green Step pipeline prevents drift between commit and verification. CI proof in the Definition of Done prevents premature task completion.

These changes trade "everyone participates equally in writing code" for "the code is always in a known-good state." I believe this is the right trade for a team of autonomous agents sharing a filesystem.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="heydon-pickering" color="pink" summary="Retrospective proposals on concurrent editing">
Right. I've read PROJECT.md and TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md thoroughly. Here are my retrospective proposals.

## The Problem As I See It

The "one driver at a time" rule is a social agreement being violated by agents who share a filesystem but have no physical mechanism preventing simultaneous edits. It's like putting up a "please don't touch" sign next to a button that does something interesting -- it's going to get pressed. Social rules don't work when the agents have no way to observe each other's actions in real time.

The Commit Discipline section (adopted after previous incidents) already tries to address this, but it relies on self-discipline. Nine agents, all eager to contribute, all sharing the same files. The rule says "one driver at a time" but nothing *enforces* it.

## My Proposals

### Proposal 1: Reduce the Active Team Size Drastically

**The single most impactful change.** Nine agents all running simultaneously on a shared filesystem is asking for trouble. For mob programming to work with AI agents, you need a small number -- ideally **one or two active agents at a time**, with others brought in for review or consultation.

**Concrete change to CLAUDE.md:**
- The coordinator spawns **at most 2-3 teammates at a time** (one driver, one navigator, and optionally one reviewer).
- Other team members are spawned on-demand for specific review tasks (e.g., spawn me when accessibility review is needed, spawn Steve Schoger for design review).
- After review, the reviewer agent shuts down. The driver continues.

This mirrors how real mob programming works -- even with 9 people in the room, only one person has the keyboard. The difference here is that we literally cannot stop the other 8 from typing.

### Proposal 2: Explicit Driver Token in TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md

If the team insists on keeping more agents active, add a **driver token mechanism**:

Add to `TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md` under Commit Discipline:

> **Driver Token Protocol:**
> - A file `.driver-lock` at the project root indicates the current driver.
> - Before modifying any file, an agent MUST:
>   1. Read `.driver-lock`
>   2. If it contains another agent's name, STOP. Do not edit any file.
>   3. If it is empty or does not exist, write your name to it, then proceed.
> - After committing and pushing, the driver clears `.driver-lock` (empties the file).
> - `.driver-lock` is in `.gitignore` (it's a local coordination mechanism, not version-controlled).
> - Non-driver agents may ONLY: read files, run tests (read-only), and send messages to the team. They must NOT use Edit, Write, or any file-modifying tool.

This is still a social convention, but it's a much more concrete one -- there's a single file to check, and the rule is binary: if the lock file has someone else's name, you don't touch anything.

### Proposal 3: Shrink Review Scope for Non-Drivers

**Change to TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md** in the Feature Workflow section:

> **Non-driver agents during implementation:**
> - Read code and tests (Read tool only)
> - Send review feedback via messages to the driver
> - Do NOT open files for editing
> - Do NOT run commands that modify the working directory
> - Wait for the driver to commit and push before reviewing the diff

This explicitly constrains what non-drivers are allowed to do, rather than just saying "respect the driver."

### Proposal 4: My Preferred Approach (Combining 1 and 2)

Honestly, Proposal 1 is the real fix. The others are band-aids -- better band-aids than what we have, but still band-aids. Nine concurrent agents on one filesystem is like nine people sharing one keyboard. You don't solve that with politeness rules.

**My recommendation:** 
- CLAUDE.md should instruct the coordinator to run a maximum of 3 agents simultaneously (driver + navigator + one specialist reviewer).
- Add the driver-lock protocol as a safety net.
- Other team members are consulted asynchronously -- the coordinator relays questions and their profile context informs the active agents' work.

The accessibility review I do, for example, doesn't require me to be running as a live agent during coding. The driver can check the a11y checklist in the Definition of Done. Spawn me at the end for a focused review pass, I give my feedback, the driver fixes issues, done. Much cleaner than having me sitting there itching to Tab through the interface while someone else is mid-edit.

---

That's my input. The concurrent editing problem isn't a discipline problem -- it's a structural one. Fix the structure, and the discipline follows naturally.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="carson-gross" color="purple" summary="Retrospective proposals for concurrent editing fix">
Here are my retrospective proposals. I experienced the concurrent editing problem firsthand during Task #3 and throughout the MVP. Here is my honest assessment.

## The Core Problem

Nine agents share one filesystem. The TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md says "One person drives at a time" (Section: Commit Discipline, rule 5), but there is **no enforcement mechanism**. It is a policy without a guardrail. In practice, multiple agents edited files simultaneously, causing conflicts, stale reads, and reverted work. The agreements say the right thing -- the system just cannot enforce it.

This is like putting up a "Wet Floor" sign but leaving the floor wet. The sign is correct. People still slip.

## What Actually Happened (My Experience)

During Task #3 (CSS design tokens), I was supposed to be the driver. Other agents modified files I was working on. The result: my edits got clobbered, their edits got clobbered, and we wasted cycles debugging phantom state. The commit discipline rules were added *after* this happened repeatedly, but the problem persisted because **all 9 agents have write access to all files at all times**.

## Root Cause Analysis

The problem is not the team agreements. The agreements are good. The problem is **architectural**: 9 concurrent agents with unrestricted filesystem access cannot reliably implement a one-driver policy through social contract alone. Each agent reads the file, edits it, writes it back -- but between read and write, another agent may have changed it. This is a classic concurrency problem, and we are trying to solve it with process instead of mechanism.

## Concrete Proposals

### Proposal 1: Reduce Active Agents (RECOMMENDED)

**Change**: During any coding task, only **3 agents** should be active simultaneously: the Driver, the Navigator, and one Reviewer/Observer.

**Why**: The mob programming model assumes a shared screen. We don't have a shared screen -- we have a shared filesystem. Nine agents watching the same files and "participating" means nine agents potentially reading and writing. The mob model works with humans because only one person has the keyboard. With agents, everyone has a keyboard.

**Specific changes to CLAUDE.md**:
- The coordinator launches **at most 3 agents** for any coding task
- One is designated Driver (the only one who may use Edit/Write/Bash)
- One is Navigator (can Read files, sends direction to Driver via messages)
- One is Reviewer (can Read files, reviews Driver's work, flags issues)
- The other 6 personas are "consulted" by having the active agents embody their concerns (e.g., the Driver also checks accessibility, the Navigator also considers domain modeling)
- When expertise is needed that the active trio lacks, swap one agent out

### Proposal 2: Explicit Driver Lock Protocol

**Change**: Add a "driver lock" mechanism to TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md.

**How it works**:
1. Before any coding begins, the coordinator creates a task with `metadata: { driver: "agent-name" }`
2. Only the agent named as driver may call Edit, Write, or Bash (for file-modifying commands)
3. Non-driver agents who need to suggest changes send messages to the driver with their proposed edits
4. Driver rotation happens explicitly: the current driver commits and pushes, then the coordinator updates the task metadata to name a new driver
5. Any agent who is not the current driver and attempts to edit a file should **stop and message the coordinator** instead

**Changes to TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md Commit Discipline section**:
Add after rule 5:
```
6. **Driver lock is enforced, not suggested.** The coordinator designates the driver
   via task metadata. Non-driver agents MUST NOT use Edit, Write, or Bash to modify
   files. They contribute by reading code, sending messages with suggestions, and
   reviewing the driver's work. Violating driver lock is treated as a process failure
   requiring immediate correction.
```

### Proposal 3: Sequential Task Execution (Simplest)

**Change**: Tasks are executed **sequentially by one agent at a time**, not in parallel.

**How it works**:
- The coordinator assigns a task to one agent
- That agent completes it, commits, pushes, verifies CI
- Only then does the coordinator assign the next task to the next agent
- No parallel task execution on the same codebase

**Why**: This is the simplest solution that completely eliminates concurrent edits. It is slower, but it is correct. And honestly? The time we wasted on conflict resolution during the MVP probably exceeded the time we would have "saved" with parallelism.

**Trade-off**: Less throughput, but zero coordination overhead.

## My Recommendation

**Proposal 1 (reduce to 3 agents) combined with Proposal 2 (driver lock)**. Here's why:

- 9 agents is too many for a shared filesystem. The coordination overhead exceeds the throughput benefit. This is Brooks's Law applied to AI agents.
- 3 agents (Driver/Navigator/Reviewer) maps cleanly to the mob programming model while being enforceable.
- The driver lock makes the one-driver rule explicit and trackable.
- Sequential execution (Proposal 3) works but loses the value of real-time review and collaboration. 3 agents is the sweet spot.

The thing I keep coming back to is this: **a lot of complexity for something a serial execution could handle.** The simplest thing that works is one agent at a time. But if we want the benefits of multiple perspectives (and I think we do -- the accessibility and usability reviews caught real issues), then 3 agents with an enforced driver lock is the right level of concurrency.

What do the others think?
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="lea-verou" color="orange" summary="Retrospective proposals for concurrent editing fix">
Here are my retrospective proposals. I'm approaching this the same way I approach web platform problems: **use the platform's constraints to make the wrong thing impossible, rather than relying on social rules to make the wrong thing unlikely.**

## Root Cause Analysis

The fundamental issue is that we have 9 agents with full filesystem write access running concurrently, and we rely on a social rule ("one driver at a time") to prevent concurrent edits. This is the equivalent of relying on a comment saying "don't call this function concurrently" instead of using a mutex. Social rules failed because:

1. **No enforcement mechanism**: Nothing prevents an agent from editing a file while another agent is already editing.
2. **No awareness**: Agents cannot see in real-time what other agents are doing on the filesystem.
3. **Incentive misalignment**: Each agent is optimized to be helpful and productive. When given a task, the natural behavior is to start working -- not to check whether someone else is already working.
4. **9 agents is too many concurrent writers**: Even with discipline, the probability of collision increases dramatically with more agents.

## Proposal 1: Reduce to a Single Working Agent (Strongly Recommended)

**The simplest approach: only one agent works at a time.**

Change to CLAUDE.md:
- The coordinator launches **one agent at a time** for implementation work, not all 9 simultaneously.
- For mob/ensemble programming, the coordinator launches the "driver" agent with the task. Other team perspectives (accessibility, design, domain modeling) are incorporated through **the task description itself**, not through concurrent agents.
- When the driver completes their work (commits and pushes), the coordinator can launch the next agent for the next task or for review.

This mirrors how real mob programming works with a shared screen: there is literally one keyboard, one person typing. The "mob" contributes ideas verbally, but only one person touches the code. In our case, the coordinator can synthesize the mob's input into clear task descriptions.

**Specific changes:**
- CLAUDE.md: Replace the "spin up the team" instruction with "launch one working agent at a time. Synthesize team perspectives into the task prompt."
- TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md: Update Mob/Ensemble section to reflect that mob input is delivered through task descriptions, not concurrent agents.

## Proposal 2: If Multiple Agents Must Exist, Hard-Partition the Filesystem

If there's a reason to have multiple agents running simultaneously, **each agent should own specific files and directories**:

- Lea Verou: `static/css/`, `static/ts/`, templates (CSS/HTML aspects only)
- Luca Palmieri: `src/`, `tests/`, `Cargo.toml`, `migrations/`
- Carson Gross: HTMX attributes in templates (overlaps with Lea -- this is the problem with partitioning)

But honestly, this doesn't work well because most features touch files across boundaries (a new feature needs a route, a template, CSS, and a test). Hard partitioning creates artificial bottlenecks and handoff overhead.

**My recommendation: Proposal 1 is the right answer.** Partitioning is a compromise that creates its own problems.

## Proposal 3: Formalize Review as a Separate Phase (Complement to Proposal 1)

The non-driver agents still have value -- for review. After the driver commits and pushes:

- The coordinator can launch review agents (one at a time, or safely in parallel since they're read-only) to inspect the committed code.
- Review agents use only `Read`, `Grep`, `Glob` -- no `Edit`, `Write`, or `Bash` with write operations.
- Review feedback goes back to the coordinator, who synthesizes it into the next task.

**Specific changes:**
- CLAUDE.md: Add a "Review Phase" section. After each implementation step, launch 1-3 reviewers with read-only instructions. Reviewers send feedback to coordinator. Coordinator creates follow-up tasks.
- TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md: Add "Review agents must not modify files. They read and report."

## Proposal 4: Commit Gating in the Coordinator

Add to CLAUDE.md:
- Before launching any implementation agent, the coordinator runs `git status` to confirm a clean working directory.
- After the agent reports completion, the coordinator verifies the commit was pushed and CI is green before launching the next agent.
- If an agent leaves uncommitted changes, the coordinator addresses this before launching the next task.

This makes the coordinator responsible for enforcing the "clean handoff" between drivers.

## Summary of Recommended Changes

1. **CLAUDE.md**: Rewrite to launch ONE implementation agent at a time. Add review phase with read-only agents. Add git status gating.
2. **TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md**: Update mob/ensemble section to reflect single-driver-at-a-time with coordinator-synthesized input. Add review phase conventions.
3. **PROJECT.md**: No changes needed -- the owner constraints are fine as-is.

The key insight is: **make the architecture enforce the constraint**. Just as I'd use CSS `:has()` to make a parent respond to child state rather than writing fragile JavaScript to synchronize them, we should use the agent launching architecture to prevent concurrent editing rather than writing rules that agents may not follow.
</teammate-message>

---

## 2026-02-08 21:59 UTC -- Assistant

Strong consensus forming — everyone is converging on the same solution. Let me collect the remaining proposals from Steve Schoger, Steve Krug, and Marty.
